Regarding the Visit of the British Industrial Mission to Manchuria 94

Publication of Correspondence between the British Industries Federation and Envoy Guo

Envoy Guo Also Lodges a Protest with the British Foreign Office

A London special correspondent for the North China Daily News reported on October 30th that the publication of correspondence between Lord Scott, Chairman of the British Industries Federation, and Guo Taiqi, the Chinese Envoy to Britain, contained acrimonious revelations and gave rise to pointed criticism.

Lord Scott wrote to Envoy Guo on August 9th as follows: "Your Excellency, the British Industries Federation has resolved to send a small mission to examine the commercial conditions in Manchuria and Japan, which you may already know. I enclose a copy of the notice which will shortly appear in the newspapers. It would be most gratifying if the mission could have the opportunity to visit China, but the mission's time does not permit this. However, I particularly hope that Mr. Bigot, representing the British steel industry, will be able to visit China to discuss certain issues related to his industry." Envoy Guo replied as follows: "Your Lordship, I have received your letter of August 9th, informing me that your Federation will send a mission to Manchuria and Japan. I express my sincere gratitude for your courtesy and good intentions. I also understand that you hope that Mr. Bigot, representing the steel industry, will be able to visit our country to discuss certain issues related to his industry. I must express my regret that the entire mission cannot spare time to visit our country, for even though our country has temporarily lost Manchuria, all goodwill and markets are of great benefit and value to industrialists and manufacturers in the Far East. I am confident that you share this sentiment. I dare say that the existing and potential British investments in the Chinese market are worthy of your Federation's attention and following, purely from a trade perspective and without involving the clear legal and moral disputes contained in the current secession of the puppet Manchuria from China. Our country's newspapers have expressed great concern upon hearing the news of your mission's visit to Manchuria and Japan. After receiving your letter, I conveyed my concerns to your Foreign Office. Unfortunately, these concerns have been confirmed by news reports from our country. Moreover, regardless of the negative repercussions that this may cause to our country, it must be stated that in areas where Japanese power is strong, trade opportunities for other countries besides Japan are indeed very limited. In the past two years, foreign firms in Manchuria, including those from your country, have been forced to close down. Reputable British companies, such as the Kailan Mining Administration, have suffered great losses due to Japanese interference and discrimination. The special dispatch from Dalian published in the Times on Saturday, August 11th, clearly shows how and why such incidents are unavoidable due to the Japanese. In today's puppet Manchuria, the open-door policy is nominally a political principle, but in reality, it is just empty talk. This has already been proven in writing. As the Chinese Envoy to London, it is my duty to protect and enhance the good understanding between the people of our country and the businessmen of your country, just as it is my duty to promote good understanding between our government and the government to which I am accredited. Therefore, I must frankly express my opinion that, from a long-term perspective, this mission is unlikely to achieve its desired results. Trade in the Far East must be achieved and distributed through sincere cooperation. This cooperation contains many factors. We all regard the great market of China not only as the cornerstone of Asian trade but also as a large part of the arch itself. I have no doubt about this. It is the real understanding and cooperation in this great mutual undertaking that will ultimately benefit your country's shipping and commerce. This is what British and Chinese businessmen and people should strive for. I believe that you will agree with my views. Politics are easily influenced by trade and can also influence trade. If so, then China is not only the center of Asian trade but also the center of Asian politics."

Lord Scott replied to Envoy Guo as follows: "I am most grateful for your letter of the 14th of this month. I assure Your Excellency that the British Industries Federation is deeply aware of the importance of trade between China and Britain and is willing to continue its past efforts in every way to encourage friendly trade relations between the people of the two countries. You must be aware of the various steps we have already taken in this regard, especially the various facilities we have provided to Chinese trade students to enable them to continue their business studies in our country. I am pleased that this plan was initiated by us. We are very satisfied with the results of this initiative, as it has shown various prospects for expanding its scope and becoming a valuable channel for mutual contact between business circles. We sincerely hope to continue our efforts to maintain the most friendly trade relations with your country. I can assure Your Excellency that anything the Federation can do in this regard will be greatly welcomed by me as its chairman." It is reported that Envoy Guo later lodged a protest with the British Foreign Office, opposing the dispatch of this mission to Manchuria. The British Foreign Office replied that the Foreign Office had not been involved in this matter and that it was purely a commercial endeavor with no political implications. Regarding this matter, although no announcement has been made, it is said that Envoy Guo does not accept this view.

The mission then departed, which is well known. The newspapers this week have all reported on the remarks made by Lord Barnby, the leader of the mission, on the eve of his departure from Tokyo. Baron Eyoh, Chairman of the Japan Economic Association, also left Tokyo for Manchuria. Lord Barnby's remarks were as follows: "As a result of harmonious discussions between leading representatives of the Japanese business and commercial world and the British industrial mission, it has been agreed in principle that committees of the Japan Economic Association and the British Industries Federation should be established in Tokyo and London to discuss issues relating to the industries and commerce of both countries with a view to arriving at a satisfactory solution. It was also agreed that the Japan Economic Association and the British Industries Federation should be invited to implement this type of project in a continuous manner in order to promote mutually beneficial trade relations between Japan and Britain."

A London correspondent for the Daily Mail once wrote that "the Japanese really want to obtain bank loans in 'Manchukuo'. The political reasons for this are even greater than the financial reasons. Sir Seligman has openly informed the Japanese side that 'the opinion of the responsible parties in Britain' (Sir Seligman's remarks probably refer to the opinion of the banking community) is now in favor of the revival of the Anglo-Japanese alliance. It is now being discussed that this financial assistance should first be obtained through private banking channels, but later this loan should be consolidated, and public bonds should be issued in the London market. It is said that the Japanese side is particularly keen on this, as they believe that obtaining direct concern for 'Manchukuo' from ordinary British investors would be of great political benefit to the Japanese."

Since Sir Seligman made the above remarks in Tokyo, I (the correspondent referring to himself) therefore add a piece of news heard on Friday's Daily Mail, which I believe can be regarded as very accurate.

The words and deeds of Lord Barnby, Sir Seligman, and their colleagues in the British Industries Federation mission in Tokyo have caused great consternation in London political circles. It has been stated in advance that the mission has no official status and no right to discuss any political issues between Britain and Japan. Therefore, even if it is undertaken in a semi-official capacity, it is not possible. But after Lord Barnby spoke of linking Britain and "Manchukuo" into a chain of friendship, he added, "The British government is well aware of our purpose and has given us various encouragements." It is no wonder that Tokyo views this as "probing opinions."

Bandit Suppression on the Henan-Hubei-Anhui Border, Bandits Fleeing West Across the Pinghan Railway 95

General Headquarters Orders Administrative Commissioners to Handle Relief Work

Hankou Correspondence: The pseudo 25th and 28th Armies have been harassing the border areas of the three provinces of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui since 1932, and their momentum has been great. Although they have been severely suppressed several times, they have not been fundamentally eliminated. Recently, according to the news released by the Bandit Suppression Headquarters of the three provinces, since Chairman Chiang came to Hankou in October and convened the generals of the three provinces to give instructions in person, Shangguan Yunxiang was appointed as the commander of the pursuit and suppression team, which was divided into five detachments. On October 15th, they began to jointly suppress the bandits. At that time, the bandits' strength was about 3,000 men with more than 2,000 guns. However, the officers and soldiers of the National Army fought bravely and took the lead, so they were able to repeatedly annihilate the strong enemy. The Pei and Wang detachments killed more than 300 bandits in the battle of Taojiahe on October 27th. The bandits knew that their future was precarious, so they fled erratically, trying to avoid battle, while the National Army followed closely, leaving no room for respite. In the battle of Hongqishan on November 4th, the Hao detachment and Wang brigade killed more than 600 bandits and dispersed the bandits' baggage and coolie teams, women's teams, etc. The remaining bandits became even more embarrassed. On November 8th, they fled to the Yunwu Mountain area of Guangshan County in an attempt to resist stubbornly by occupying the mountain, but were trapped. However, before the bandits could climb to the mountainside, the Xing and Liu detachments had already arrived, and the two sides engaged in hand-to-hand combat. The fierceness of the battle was rare. In this battle, 600 to 700 bandits were killed. The remaining bandits buried all the wounded and sick bandits alive and fled west in a panic, carrying only pseudo-important political personnel. In order to eliminate the root of the problem, our pursuit and suppression teams continued to pursue them in formation. In the battle of Luoguzhai on the 16th, the Liu detachment killed more than 100 bandits. The remaining bandits, numbering less than 1,000, crossed the Pinghan Railway to the west on November 17th, with the intention of entering Sichuan and Shaanxi. They are currently being relentlessly pursued and intercepted by the National Army's pursuit teams and local garrisons. The bandits are at the end of their rope, and the day of annihilation should not be far off. As for the relief work, the General Headquarters has submitted a request to the Xingying, which will be handled by the administrative commissioners. In addition, in the Yangrui border area between Hubei and Jiangxi, there was also the pseudo-newly編團. After being severely suppressed by the various units of the Third Column of the Western Route Army, the bandit leader Zou Zhimu was captured, and Zhang Tao went missing. The remaining 200 to 300 people were scattered and hidden. Recently, they were collected by Liu Yonghong and others in the Yangshugang area and formed into two battalions. On the 17th of this month, the National Army's Zhang Liansan Brigade heard the news and advanced to suppress them. They happened to be holding an enlarged meeting in Zhangjia, Qingshan,召集ed bandits from northern Jiangxi and Longhu and Rui, so they were given a severe blow. Two pseudo-guerrilla captains, Xiang Yushan and Shen Gengtong, were captured alive, and one pseudo-regiment commander, Wu Ying, and more than ten bandits were killed. More than 20 rifles were seized. The remaining bandits fled in panic towards Yangduan and are still being tracked down. As for the remnants of He Long's bandit forces on the border of Hubei and Hunan, they once infiltrated Yongshun in western Hunan, but were recovered by the Hunan Army's Chen Quzhen Division. The remnants fled towards Sangzhi, attempting to infiltrate western Hubei. The large army of Xu Yuanquan's troops is blocking the key areas, and it is determined that they will not cross the Leichi border.

Overall, the current bandit suppression situation is that the old nest of the Jiangxi bandits has been completely destroyed, and the military operation can be concluded. There are less than 1,000 remaining bandits on the border of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui, and it is also expected that they will be completely eliminated. (23rd)

Coal Mine Survey in Various Counties of Henan Province 96

Reserves Rank Fourth in the Country

Sufficient for 3,500 Years of Mining

Kaifeng Correspondence: The coal reserves in various counties of Henan Province are about 9,401,080,000 tons. Except for Shanxi, Shaanxi, and Sichuan, no other province can compare. The production area covers about 1,734 square kilometers, and the annual output is only 2,570,000 tons, accounting for only 0.0273% of the reserves. According to the current mining rate, it is sufficient for 3,500 years of mining. Therefore, the coal industry in Henan is just beginning to flourish. The following is a description of the current situation of various coal mines recently obtained by the Geological Survey Institute, divided by region, for the reference of those who are concerned about the coal industry.

(1) Xiubo Coalfield Area: Includes the areas of Xiuwu and Boai counties, as well as parts of Qinyang and Jiyuan. The most notable is the Zhongfu Joint Office, which was formed in June 1933 by the Zhongyuan Coal Mine Company and the British Fook Company. It is divided into two major mining plants, called the First Mining Plant (East Plant) and the Second Mining Plant (West Plant). The Zhongyuan Company of the East Plant is located in the Panlonghe Village area, 40 miles northwest of Xiuwu County, and the Fook Company of the West Plant is located in the Wangfeng Lifeng area, 50 miles northeast of Boai County. The two plants are about 30 miles apart from east to west. The output in the first half of the year was 487,620 tons. In the past, the monthly shortfall was more than 100,000 tons. In September, Weng Wenhao and Zhang Jingyu奉命ed by Chairman Chiang to rectify the situation, reduce improper expenses, and lay off employees, and it gradually got on track. The second is the Minyou Coal Mine in Boai, which is located in Houxinzhuang near Changkou Station on the Daoqing Road. It covers an area of about 10 hectares and 11 acres and has eight coal wells with a daily output of 500 tons. Furthermore, the Zhenxing Coal Mine in Jiyuan County is located in Kejing Village in the county. It covers an area of 88 hectares and 36 acres and is currently closed.

(2) Anyang Coalfield Area: Includes the Anyang, Wu'an, Tangyin, Linxian, Jixian, and Qixian areas. (A) Liuhegou Coal Mine is located 60 miles northwest of Anyang County. A branch road has been built to connect it with the Pinghan Railway. It covers an area of 1,280 hectares and 22 acres, with a current daily output of 1,600 tons. (B) Yi'an Coal Mine is located in Xiabao, Shuizhi Town, 45 miles west of Anyang. It covers an area of 74 hectares and 48 acres, with a daily output of 170 tons. (C) Dachang Coal Mine is located in Dacheng Village, 16 miles southwest of Shuizhi Town in Anyang. It covers an area of 128 hectares and 73 acres, with a daily output of 80 tons. (D) Zhonghe Coal Mine is located in Wayaogou, Anyang. It covers an area of 52 hectares and 30 acres. It is currently being repaired due to the窯bottom being flooded. (E) Dacheng Coal Mine is located in Zhaoxian Village, Gedashan, 20 miles east of Wu'an City. It covers an area of 9,322 acres, with a daily output of 140 to 150 tons of coal. (F) Dingsheng Coal Mine is located in Huyu Village, Wu'an. It has recently been shut down due to lack of profits. (G) Yihe Coal Mine is located in Xiaosiwan, Tangyin. It covers an area of 955.75 acres, with a daily output of 40 tons. (H) Jiuhua Coal Mine is located in Hebi Town, Tangyin. It covers an area of 9,533.15 acres, with a daily output of 40 to 50 tons. (I) Gucheng Coal Mine is also located in Hebi Town, Tangyin. It covers an area of 18 hectares and 71 acres and is currently being developed. (J) Dashun Coal Mine is located in Lingji Village, Linxian. It covers an area of 187 hectares and has not yet officially produced coal.

(3) Xin’an  Coalfield Area: Starting from Xin'an in the east to Shanxian in the west, the largest coal mine is the Minsheng Company in Guanyintang, Shanxian. It covers an area of 303 hectares and 21 acres, with a daily output of 200 tons of coal. Recently, an 8-meter-thick coal seam has been discovered, which is very promising. The Xin'an Coal Mine is located in Shang Gudeng Village, Qiugou, northwest of Xin'an. It is currently closed. The Yuqing Coal Mine has also been changed to a leasing property due to poor business.

(4) Yumi Coalfield Area: Yumi County is the main part, including the eastern part of Dengfeng and the northern part of Jia County. (A) Sanfeng Coal Mine is located on Sanfeng Mountain, southwest of Yu County. It covers an area of 195 hectares and 43 acres, with a daily output of 240 to 250 tons. (B) Jizhong Coal Mine is located on Yuhuang Mountain, south of Yu County. The output of coal is very small. (C) Fan Jiazhuang Coal Mine is located in Fan Jiazhuang, Qihua Town, Miyi County. It covers an area of 1,378.40 acres and is mined using local methods. (C) Yufeng Coal Mine is located in Lishuwa, Chaohua Town, Miyi County. It covers an area of 1,461.60 acres. (D) Tongxin Coal Mine is located in Xiaolizhai, east of Miyi County. It covers an area of 1,475.76 acres, with a daily output of 200 tons. (E) Minsheng Coal Mine is located in Lishi Yagou, northwest of Miyi County. It covers an area of 1,470.83 acres. (F) Demao Coal Mine is located outside the west gate of Miyi County. It covers an area of 544.70 acres and is very small in scale. (G) Tongxing Coal Mine is located in Chenlou Village, Dengfeng. It covers an area of 8 hectares and 31 acres. (H) Tongqing Coal Mine is located in Bailiping, Dengfeng. It has not been in operation for two years. (I) Haogou Coal Mine is located in Haogou, Dengfeng. It covers an area of 10 hectares and 4 acres, with a daily output of 50 tons in the旺busy months.

(5) Yiluo Coalfield Area: Distributed in Yiyang, Luoyang, Yanshi, Gongxian and other counties. (A) Dadong Coal Mine is located in Magou near Shuitou, 50 miles southeast of Gong County. It covers an area of 149,648 acres and is currently closed due to being exhausted. (B) Fuju Coal Mine is located in Shengshui Village, Gong County. It covers an area of 1,665.27 acres, with a daily output of 60 tons. (C) Xiesheng Coal Mine is located in the south of Jinfang Mountain, Yiyang. It covers an area of 6 hectares and 10 acres, with a daily output of 90 tons. (D) Zhonghua Coal Mine is located in Jishuping, Yiyang. It covers an area of 1,033.78 acres, with a daily output of 70 tons.

(6) Rubao Coalfield Area: Distributed in Linru, Baofeng, and Lushan counties. Currently, the Zhengyi Coal Mine in Zhangbaqiao, Baofeng, is engaged in mining. It covers an area of 137 hectares and 97 acres, with a daily output of 60 tons.

(7) Nantai Coalfield Area: Distributed in Nantai County. No one has yet mined it.

(8) Shanggu Coalfield Area: Located in Shangcheng and Gushi counties. It has not yet been mined. Other coal mines that have obtained licenses but have not been mined include Xiaoxuzhuang Coal Mine in Boai, Wanshengpo Coal Mine in Wu'an, Xiaozhuang Coal Mine and Shiguoshan Coal Mine in Yu County, two mines belonging to Fenghuang in Tangyin, Xiaocun Coal Mine and Litonggou Coal Mine in Xin'an, Sunzhai Village Coal Mine in Gong County, and Sanyuan Village Coal Mine in Dengfeng. Decline of Commerce in Guangdong Province 97

Commercial Depression, Industrial Crash

Poor Local Products, Trade Deficit

Guangzhou Correspondence: The commercial situation in Guangdong Province has been very poor recently. Large stores in Guangzhou City have been closing down from time to time. The main reason is the sluggish business, the weak purchasing power of the people, and the depletion of funds in the market, which has led to a crash in industry. Taishan and other counties have always been known as prosperous areas, but recently, due to a sharp reduction in the inflow of foreign capital and the unemployment of many overseas Chinese who have returned to the country, the market has been greatly affected. The bankruptcy of silver firms and merchants has also been seen several times. Shantou is an important trading port, but in recent years, it has been affected by the recession overseas, and the financial situation is extremely difficult. Since the financial turmoil occurred in the market, it has not yet returned to its original state. Although the issuance of market merchant treasury certificates has maintained it for a while, there is still no way to clear the bills issued by silver firms. Overall, the economic situation in various places is very pessimistic.

As for Guangdong Province's foreign trade, from January to September of this year, according to the statistics of various customs offices, the province's trade deficit reached more than 64 million yuan (according to the statistics of the Guangdong Provincial Investigation and Statistics Bureau). This leakage is truly alarming. During these nine months, the total import of foreign goods was 120,508,925 yuan, and the total export of local goods was 57,857,718 yuan. Comparing the two, the trade deficit was 64,661,207 yuan. The following is a list of the import and export statistics of foreign trade by customs office from January to September:

Wujiang 101

Zhao Zhiping Arrested in Zhejiang

Zhao Zhiping, son of Zhao Yongcai, a Henan native residing in this county, is thirty years old. Wuxi 102

Anhui Refugees Rob and Assault People

Recently, Su County, Anhui, has experienced a famine year, resulting in groups of people fleeing the disaster, mostly professional refugees. A group of over 150 refugees from Su County arrived in Wuxi from Changzhou the other day and were lodging in the Yansheng Temple in Lihua Zhuang. The Sixth Sub-Bureau of the Public Security Bureau was notified and immediately dispatched armed police to suppress them. Yesterday morning, at approximately 10:00 AM, the refugees attempted to detour through Zhangshe Hudi to Suzhou when they passed by the Yin Lane area of Chao Yin Township in the Second District. They went to the home of villager Wu Yongquan and forcibly stole two hens and several stones of rice. When the villagers reasoned with them, they were brutally beaten. Tang Wenzhen, the Tu Zheng (local leader), and villagers Wu Juhe and Tang Liangbao were all injured. A man named A Er was also severely beaten by the refugees and is said to have had his spine broken, endangering his life. The injured have been rushed to the hospital for treatment. All the refugees have been intercepted by the Wangting Merchant Corps, pending a report to the county government for processing.

Farmers’ Appeal Regarding Distilling Alcohol

Farmers in the Huadafangzhuang area of Xin’an Township in this county are appealing against the sudden changes in regulations by Zhu Jin, the Director of the Tobacco and Alcohol License Tax Collection Office. Zhu Jin is forcibly designating farmers' by-products as business activities, forcing them to register and pay license taxes. This has led to farmers ceasing operations and collectively appealing. Distilling alcohol from rotten rice and rice mash is a utilization of waste products. Since there are no shops, how can there be license numbers? Without license numbers, how can taxes be levied? Zhu Jin is disregarding past regulations and forcibly levying taxes, which violates the sentiments of the people. According to Article 135 of the new Criminal Code, this should be punished more severely. Yesterday, Xu Shaoshan, Mo Yongsen, and sixteen others drafted seven major reasons and jointly presented them to the County Party Headquarters, requesting a telegram to be sent to the Provincial Party Headquarters, petitioning the Provincial Government to order the Finance Department, which is in charge of tax matters, to instruct the Fourth District Tobacco and Alcohol License Tax Collection Bureau to continue to handle matters according to the old regulations in order to pacify the people. Otherwise, over a thousand farming households will have no choice but to file a criminal lawsuit in accordance with the law, and meet Zhu in court, and seek compensation for losses incurred during the shutdown.

Dispute Over Casting a Bronze Statue of a Past Sage

Mr. Hu Yuren, a past sage of this county, was highly respected for his morality and character, and was a specialist in water conservancy research. In the past, he planned the linking of rivers and lakes in this county and the opening of the West Gate Bridge, benefiting the local area. To this day, the entry and exit of lake water benefits the people of the northeast. Local people, in order to commemorate the sage and show respect, initiated a project in the seventeenth year of the Republic of China to cast a bronze statue of Mr. Hu. However, preparations have been delayed until now. During the fifth County Representative Assembly last month, it was resolved to actively prepare for the casting. Regarding the location of the statue, most people advocated placing it in the city park or by the lake. The city park has many visitors and can provide a place for admiration. The lakeside has beautiful scenery and convenient transportation, making it suitable for the viewing of domestic and foreign tourists. Mr. Hu was a water conservancy expert, and his achievements were in water conservancy, making the lakeside a more meaningful place to erect the statue. However, a few people from Yanqiao Township, considering Yanqiao to be Mr. Hu's hometown, insisted on placing the statue in the countryside, which would defeat the purpose of commemorating the sage, resulting in a dispute that has not yet been resolved.

Merchant Corps Captures Four Thieves

Wu Weian, the captain of the Thirty-First Brigade of the Donghutang Merchant Corps, led over ten members on patrol in the Yangshuxia area on the morning of the other day, arresting four thieves named Gu Genpei, Zhang Tongfu, Gu Agui, and Chen Jinsheng. Under questioning, they confessed to robbing Gu Guichun's home in November of last year, and Gu Yinsheng's home on October 14th of this year, and using the stolen goods. Yesterday (the 24th), Captain Wu submitted a document to the Merchant Corps Guild, which transferred them to the county government for interrogation.

It is now known that all of the seeds have been transported to Changshu, totaling 1,200 shi. The distribution method is as follows: the Sixth District, being the hardest hit, receives 700 dan; the Second District receives 300 dan; and the Fifth District, having purchased their own seeds, receives only 200 dan. After the above plan is approved by the general assembly on the 23rd, it will be distributed to each district for farmers to sow, hoping for a harvest next spring to compensate for their losses.

Ningbo 109

Water Police Squad Uncovers a Large Bandit Gang

The Yongping gunboat, under the command of the Second Squadron of the Water Police, was dispatched to patrol the ocean on the 18th. At approximately 4:00 PM that afternoon, while patrolling the waters east of Putuo, they suddenly saw two sailboats speeding away. Suspecting their behavior, the gunboat immediately followed them and pursued them to the east and west gates of Xidong Mountain. The ships had already docked at the shore and the people on board were disembarking. Knowing that it was undoubtedly a bandit den, the gunboat immediately radioed the squadron headquarters and requested additional support from the Xinbaoshun patrol boat to encircle and suppress them. However, after searching for two days and nights, no trace of the bandits was found. Later, fishermen revealed that the bandits were hiding in a cave on the coast. The officers fired warning shots near the cave and ordered the bandits to come out, or they would be killed. The bandits, seeing the urgency of the situation and having been besieged for two days and nights, had no power to resist and came out of the cave, surrendering themselves. A total of twenty-one bandits were captured. Two of them jumped into the sea while being bound, leaving nineteen captured. Three refugees were rescued. Eight White Wave brand pistols and ten rifles were seized, along with ammunition. They were sent to the squadron headquarters for interrogation.

Local News

Central and Five Other Banks Negotiate Loan to Anhui Province 110

Total Loan of 1.2 Million Yuan

Salt Surplus as Guarantee, Three Installments

The Anhui Provincial Government is borrowing a total of 1.2 million yuan from the Central and five other banks in Shanghai. After Director Mao negotiated with the banks in Shanghai, they reconvened at 4:00 PM yesterday and reached an agreement. The contract is being drafted. The details are as follows:

Suspension of Treasury Bond Issuance: The Anhui Provincial Treasury has suffered from the impact of the drought, leading to a sharp decline in revenue and a budget deficit. A request was submitted to the Central Government for permission to issue 900,000 yuan in local treasury bonds for the 23rd year of the Republic of China. This was approved, and the regulations were passed by the Legislative Yuan. When Director of Finance Mao Longzhang came to Shanghai this time, he negotiated with various banks. For the sake of procedural convenience, the approved treasury bonds will be suspended from printing and issuing. Instead, a loan will be taken from the banks within the scope of the 900,000 yuan treasury bond principle.

Five Banks Undertake the Loan: The above loan will be guaranteed by the collateral stipulated in the treasury bond regulations, namely, the salt surplus allocated to the province by the Ministry of Finance. After Director Mao negotiated, it was decided that the loan amount would be 800,000 yuan, to be undertaken by the Central, China, Communications, Shanghai, and China Industrial banks. Previously, the Anhui branches of the above five banks had agreed to lend 200,000 yuan to Anhui Province at the end of this lunar year and the Dragon Boat Festival of next lunar year, totaling 400,000 yuan. The above totals 1.2 million yuan.

Yesterday's Re-Meeting: Yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM, the borrowing banks reconvened on the third floor of the Central Bank on the Bund to discuss the Anhui loan. Those present included Mao Longzhang, Director of Finance of Anhui Province, Zhou Shouliang, Deputy Manager of the Shanghai Branch of the Central Bank, Zhang Peishen, Manager of the Communications Bank, and representatives from the Shanghai Bank, the Bank of China, and the China Industrial Bank, totaling six people. They dispersed at 6:00 PM.

Contract to be Signed: The total Anhui loan is 1.2 million yuan, all for government expenses. The collateral is the salt surplus allocated to the province by the Ministry of Finance. The term is twenty months from the date of the loan disbursement. It was decided to wait until the loan contract is drafted before holding another meeting to formally sign it. In the future, a general contract will be made for the 1.2 million yuan, and Director Mao will send it to Anhui after the contract is signed.

Disbursement Method: The disbursement method is as follows: The issuance of treasury bonds will be changed to a loan of 800,000 yuan, to be fully disbursed by the end of the current Gregorian year. The previously agreed loan of 400,000 yuan will be disbursed in two installments, one for 200,000 yuan at the end of this lunar year, and one for 200,000 yuan at the Dragon Boat Festival of next lunar year. The above disbursements will be made directly by the Anhui branches of the Central, China, Communications, Shanghai, and China Industrial banks to the Anhui Finance Department according to the schedule.

Striving for Lawyers to Attend the Judicial Conference 112

Petition from the National Lawyers Association

Telegram from the Shanghai Bar Association

The National Lawyers Association attaches great importance to the Judicial Conference to be convened by the Ministry of Judicial Administration in the spring of next year and advocates that the lawyer community should have representatives to participate in it, so that the judicial authorities can collect thoughts and benefit from wisdom. It is now known that the association's submission to the Ministry of Law states, in brief, that in order to seek improvements in judicial laws and regulations and to renew judicial practice, or in short, to study the increasingly perfect use of judicial power, countries around the world often gather judicial practitioners (including judges and lawyers) and legal experts to hold judicial conferences, and examples of this are too numerous to mention. The United States of America, in light of the exercise of judicial power, should be a continuous effort, and many states have permanent judicial conference institutions, so the importance of judicial conferences can be imagined. The imperfection of our country's judicial organization is undeniable. The fundamental way to improve it is to have each part of the judicial system be able to exert its effectiveness and work together. However, in order to achieve this goal, judicial practitioners from all three positions should each have complex experiences and understandings to jointly seek improvements in the exercise of judicial power. This is what reason and circumstance dictate. If this judicial conference does not have lawyer representatives participating, then the importance of the conference will be reduced, which seems to be a regret. It should be adopted by the Association, and the opinion is said.

Shanghai Lawyers Association telegraphed Minister Ju Juesheng of the Ministry of Judicial Administration yesterday, urging local lawyers associations to send representatives to participate in the judicial conference. The telegram said: Minister Ju Juesheng of the Ministry of Judicial Administration in Nanjing, I admire you very much. However, I checked that this conference did not allow lawyers to participate, which I found strange, because lawyers are members of the judicial system and have a close relationship with the exercise and improvement of judicial power. It seems inappropriate for a country ruled by law to reject them from participating. For this reason, I ask the president of the Lawyers Association to adopt and explicitly allow local lawyers associations to send representatives to participate in the conference and jointly seek improvement. The Shanghai Lawyers Association, Yao,

Portuguese Aviators Failed to Fly to Shanghai Yesterday 113

Turned Back Midway Due to Bad Weather

Portuguese young aviators Lao Baipao and Jiwa departed from Lisbon, Portugal at the end of last month on the Lai He Paide aircraft for a long-distance flight to the Far East, and have arrived in Hong Kong a few days ago. According to a telegram received by the Portuguese Consulate General in this port yesterday morning, the Portuguese aviators left Hong Kong at 7:00 AM yesterday morning to come to Shanghai, and were expected to arrive in Shanghai at 2:00 PM yesterday. Portuguese Consul General Olives, Vice Consul Ba Laika, and representatives of the Portuguese community in Shanghai were all planning to go to Hongqiao Airport for a grand welcome. However, a telegram received yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM stated that when the Portuguese aviators flew to Fuzhou, they turned back to Hong Kong due to bad weather and heavy fog, and landed safely at about 1:00 PM yesterday afternoon. As of last night, there was no definite news as to when they will depart for Shanghai again. It will depend on the weather.

The Haiheng did not arrive to Shanghai yesterday due to the fog at the Wusong Estuary. 114

Will enter the port today when the fog dissipates

The China Merchants Bureau's second new sea vessel, the Haiheng, came from England. According to a telegram received by the representative of the Shanghai British Shipyard, Maer Kang Yangxing, the ship was originally scheduled to arrive in Shanghai at 5:00 PM yesterday. The head office had sent a pilot to Tongsha to wait so that they can guide it to Shanghai. But outside the Wusong Estuary yesterday, the weather was bad and there was heavy fog on the sea. All the sea vessels from the north and south to Shanghai temporarily dropped anchor to wait for the fog to clear before entering the port. The outgoing vessels also temporarily stopped at Sanjia Water, so the Haiheng vessel could not sail to Shanghai yesterday. It will have to wait for the fog to clear today before it can sail into the Huangpu River.

Private Postal Offices Must Close by the End of the Year 115

The City Government is Ordered to Coordinate with the Post Office for Disposal

According to the Central News Agency, the City Government received an order from the Executive Yuan, which stated, in brief, that postal service is a national monopoly, which is the common practice in countries around the world. China's postal regulations are clearly stipulated, so the existence of private postal offices greatly hinders postal rights. In order to unify the postal service, the Ministry of Communications ordered the Directorate General of Posts in November of the 22nd year of the Republic of China to strictly order private postal offices in the country to gradually cease operations by the end of the 23rd year, and this was repeatedly approved by the Yuan and forwarded to provincial and municipal military and government agencies to assist the post office in cracking down on private postal offices in various places, and to end them all within the specified period. On the one hand, arrangements should be made properly before the deadline expires so that the public does not feel inconvenienced by the cancellation of private postal offices. Therefore, in light of local conditions, detailed studies should be conducted and disposed of separately according to needs, including opening more windows, adding more mail trains, increasing the number of times to collect mailboxes, extending the mail collection time, adding mailboxes and post office agencies, village and town post offices, and expanding village and town delivery, adding postal assistants, clerks, customs enforcement personnel, etc. In the future, after the private postal offices are cancelled when the deadline expires, the public will not feel any inconvenience. Therefore, although the private postal office industry has repeatedly sent representatives to petition for a delay in the ban, the Ministry of Communications believes that private postal offices hinder the government's postal rights, and the ban is inevitable. The deadline is approaching, and we should earnestly coordinate the ban, etc. After receiving the order, the City Government ordered the Social, Public Utility, and Public Security Bureaus to jointly enforce the ban.

Patriotic Youth Form a Group to Promote the Use of Domestic Goods 116

Due to the Prevalence of Inferior Goods in the Market and the Decline of Domestic Goods

Recently in this city, a group of patriotic youths, concerned about the prevalence of inferior goods in the market, the decline of domestic goods, and the resulting economic hardship and dangerous future, initiated the formation of a propaganda group to promote the use of domestic goods. After several meetings, the following organizational outline was decided: (1) This group is named the Shanghai Propaganda Group for Promoting the Use of Domestic Goods; (2) The purpose is to promote the use of domestic goods and stop the leaks; (3) Any young person in the Republic of China who has aspirations, can set an example, is introduced by two or more members, and is approved by the group, can be a member of this group; (4) The group's expenses are borne by the members themselves and will not be raised from outside; (5) The group's organization is divided into group headquarters, executive committee, investigation team, persuasion team, propaganda team, and disciplinary team; (6) All members of the group must absolutely use domestic goods for all daily necessities, such as clothing, food, and housing. If it is found that a member is using enemy goods, they will be severely warned after investigation; (7) All members of the group must absolutely obey the command of superiors and take on work separately; (8) Members of the group who work hard and have made definite achievements will be given honorary awards by the group; (9) Members of the group who disobey orders or work ineffectively will be disciplined by the group according to the severity of the case; (10) Members of the group, after joining the group, will not be allowed to leave the group permanently except for death; (11) After the group's work is completed, it may be dissolved by public announcement if it is deemed unnecessary to continue; (12) This outline will be implemented after it is announced to the members.

Currency System Research Association Establishes Office in Shanghai

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, the Ministry of Finance, considering the disorder of China's circulating currency system, has determined that it is necessary to reorganize it, and has specially organized a Currency System Committee to be responsible for studying and reforming the unified currency system. Chen Jintao, the former Minister of Finance, is appointed as the chairman of the Currency System Research Committee, and Geng Aidee, Bei Songsun, Xi Demao, Xu Xinliu, Chen Xing and other more than twenty people are hired as research committee members. Dai Mingli is invited to be the secretary-general of the association. The association has already started working in Nanjing on the 13th of this month. A few days ago, Chairman Chen Jintao came to Shanghai to consult with experts from economics, banking and other fields on the opinions on the "currency problem" recently submitted by the Ministry of Finance. The research committee members discussed this on their own, and Chen has collected the opinions of each research committee member and will return to Nanjing next week to convene a general meeting to make a final summary and decision. Furthermore, in order to facilitate the research of currency system by the committee members, the association has decided to establish an office in Shanghai. The location of the office is planned to be in the Jianghai Customs Building on the Bund, and it will start operating after the arrangement is completed. In addition, the association is actively conducting research on the decimal auxiliary currency system.

Water Management Committee Announces That Practicing Certificates Without Counter-Signature are Invalid 121

Pilot Petition Group Hosts Seafarers and the Press

Demanding Retesting for Previous Illegal Examination

The Chinese Water Management Committee announces that all pilot practice certificates issued by the Naval Department for the Song-Han District that have not been counter-signed by the Committee are invalid. The Pilot Joint Petition Group hosted various seafarer groups and the press. The details are as follows:

Announcement of Invalidity: Water Management Committee Announcement No. 4 states: In order to manage the affairs of Chinese pilots in the Song-Han District, it is hereby noted that the pilot practice certificates issued by the Naval Department last year have been successively endorsed by the Shanghai Port Authority since May 25 of this year to extend their validity. All practice certificates that have not been endorsed by the Port Authority are now invalid. Furthermore, the endorsed certificates will also be invalid if they have not been counter-signed by the chairman of the Examination Committee with the English words "Examined," "Tripserping Pilot," or "Not Examined," and "C.F.C.C" [name]. All pilot practice certificates declared invalid should be submitted to the Committee for cancellation. This announcement is hereby made for general knowledge. Furthermore, please note the articles of the Interim Pilot Management Regulations, as previously announced by the Committee, including Articles 10, 12, 13, and 14. This is announced by Chairman Canell.

Hosting Various Sectors: The Song-Han District Pilot Joint Petition Group hosted various seafarer groups and the press at the Gu Yi Xuan restaurant last night. Over twenty people attended, including representatives from seafarer groups such as the Maritime Federation, the Southern Jun'an Sailors' Association, the Yan Ying South Society, the Maritime Tiller Carpenter Mutual Aid Association, and reporters from various news agencies. The representatives of the petition group reported on the illegal examination process of the Water Management Committee, stating that pilots with excellent experience and academic ability should be guaranteed and requested permission to be retested, and hoped that various groups would provide assistance until late in the evening before dispersing.

Declaration of Defection by Three Communists 125

Luo Peiguang, Zhang Huifen, Dang Runzhi

According to the Central News Agency, Luo Peiguang, a defecting communist, is a native of Liancheng, Fujian, 26 years old, and a graduate of Great China University. He joined the Communist Party in 1932 and served as a party newspaper editor and C.Y. document officer in the Communist Party's West Shanghai District Committee. Zhang Huifen (female), a native of Yixing, Jiangsu, is 18 years old and a worker at a Shanghai West spinning mill. She joined the Communist Party in 1932 and served as an internal liaison and document custodian for the Communist Party's Jiangsu Provincial Committee. Dang Runzhi (female) is 21 years old, a native of Suide, Shaanxi, and once studied at China University in Peiping. She joined the Communist Party in 1933 and was responsible for distribution work for the Communist Party's Cultural Federation. They have now issued a declaration of defection, stating: In the past, in order to save the crisis of the nation, we did not clearly see the path that should be taken to save the nation, and mistakenly embarked on the path of communism. Subjectively, our spirit was revolutionary, but objectively, we became tools of betrayal. Now we jointly feel that the road of communism is really impossible to take. (1) The Communist Party advocates class struggle, which in fact and theory is a clumsy method of shoe-cutting for China. The class struggle in Marxism can only be suitable for countries with developed capitalism. If it is moved to China, a country with backward production, the result will inevitably be the destruction of national industry and commerce, increase the economic crisis in China, and make the entire nation move towards extinction faster. Therefore, the Communist Party's class struggle is a cruel death knell for China. (2) The nature of the Chinese revolution is still a national revolution, and only the Chinese Kuomintang can undertake and complete this great task. The Communist Party, based on the Third International's erroneous assessment, said that the Chinese revolution has reached the stage of the Soviet revolution, so they blindly organized their Soviet Red Army everywhere and carried out all their disruptive policies, causing widespread bankruptcy in rural areas and unemployment in urban areas. They do not realize their error and reverse the cause and effect, instead placing this responsibility on the Kuomintang and slandering the Kuomintang as a scourge of the country and the people. Facts speak louder than words. Who has been killing and setting fires in the interior in recent years? Who is destroying the entire anti-Japanese plan? We believe that everyone can understand and answer unanimously that the Communist Party is the criminal who destroys China and slaughters farmers and workers. (3) The only revolutionary task in China at present is to oppose the aggression of imperialism and eliminate feudal forces. To complete this arduous combat task, we can only rely on the leadership of the Chinese Kuomintang, consolidate the national front, and carry out a broad national revolution. Obviously, the forces of imperialism and feudal warlords in China are very strong. To eliminate them, we can only rely on the united front of all classes and the entire nation to have the confidence of victory. The Communist Party advocates that workers should lead. May I ask, how many industrial workers are there in China with its backward production? According to statistics, there are less than three million industrial workers in China. To complete this arduous task with this extremely small number of workers, only ghosts will believe it. People will not believe it. Therefore, we have thoroughly realized from fact and politics that communism is fundamentally impossible in China. Moreover, in fact, there are more than just the three of us who have realized the same and repented. A large number of Communist Party's lower-level cadres and even the highest-level leaders have surrendered themselves. Now, in addition to firmly turning to the banner of the Three People's Principles and striving to eradicate the Communist Party under the leadership of the Chinese Kuomintang in order to complete the task of the national revolution, we also sincerely hope that all young people who have been deceived and anesthetized by the Communist Party will also consciously come forward to surrender and accept the generous self-renewal path given to us by the central government.

Salt Administration Suspends Operation of Salt Affairs School 127

Reason is to Vigorously Reduce Administration and Cut Expenses

The School was Established Fourteen Years Ago and Had Significant Achievements

According to Xinsheng News Agency, Zhu Tingqi, Director-General of the Salt Affairs Audit Office and concurrently Director of the Salt Affairs Administration, submitted a request yesterday to suspend the operation of the Salt Affairs School. The Salt Affairs School was established in 1920 and has a history of 14 years to date. It is the only place in our country for advanced training of specialized salt affairs personnel. At a time when salt affairs are in need of reform and the government is promoting vocational education, the salt affairs authorities are actually suspending the school on the grounds of vigorously reducing administration and cutting expenses. It is a pity. The original text is excerpted as follows: "According to the Salt Affairs School's submission, regarding whether or not to continue recruiting new students in the second half of this year, please give instructions. The school was established in 1920 and was originally established to train specialized salt affairs personnel. Each year, graduates are successively distributed and employed in various salt affairs agencies. In August of last year, due to the rigorous reduction of administration and cutting of expenses in the various administrative agencies under this office, the amount was very large. If students from the school continue to graduate in the future, it will inevitably increase expenses and affect the budget. After detailed deliberation, the recruitment of new students was stopped in the second half of last year. Now, according to the submitted statement, this office re-examines the current situation. Universities in the country are becoming increasingly complete in their departments, and there are many people with expertise in public document processing and examination subjects who can be recruited and employed. It does not seem necessary to establish a special school. Furthermore, the school's expenses were originally priced by the Tuoqing Gaoxian Railway Company as a regular expense from November 1928, as instructed by the Ministry. Later, due to the company's poor business, it was unable to allocate funds as planned. The Ministry then approved a temporary allocation of 4,800 yuan per month by the Changlu Audit Branch, which was directly transferred to the school for use from January 1932 until now. This allocation is temporary in nature, and the amount allocated over the years is considerable. The Changlu salt funds are currently being reorganized, and it seems that savings should be planned in advance to prepare for future contributions. Based on the above reasons, it is proposed that after the school's current third-year and original second-year classes graduate (the third-year class will graduate in the first half of this year, and the second-year class will graduate in the first half of next year), the school should be closed to conclude operations. Before the closure, it is proposed to reduce the school's 1934 expenses to 3,000 yuan per month, which will still be allocated monthly by the Changlu Audit Office. In addition to the school's request regarding whether to recruit students in the second half of this year, it is proposed that this office instruct to stop recruiting students from the second half of this year. The reasons for the school's planned closure by the first half of 1935 are presented in writing for your review."

After getting off the train, he went directly to his friend's house at 262 Shanzhong Road to rest. The local American community is scheduled to host a banquet to welcome him that evening. Ambassador Bullitt plans to stay in Shanghai for three or four days and is scheduled to leave Shanghai and return to the United States on the President McKinley of the Da Lai Shipping Company on the morning of the 27th. He was originally scheduled to fly to Guangzhou for sightseeing from Shanghai on the 25th, but now it is too late, and the trip has been cancelled.

Pudong Electric Company Supplies Power to Nanhui County Towns 131

The Pudong Electric Company has been actively constructing and expanding in recent years. In addition to the areas along the Pudong River belonging to Shanghai Municipality, including Gaoqiao, Gaohang, Luhang, Yangjing, Tangqiao, Yangsi, and the Sixth District, as well as Sanlin and Chenhang in the Shanghai County, where poles and wires have long been installed and electricity is widely supplied, they have also been gradually expanding to the neighboring Nanhui and Chuansha counties. For example, Beicai, Zhangjiangzha, the Fujia Catholic Church, Chen Tuiguan Bridge, Sun Xiaoqiao, Hengmian, etc., in the Fourth District of Nanhui County, and Tangmu Bridge Town in Chuansha County, are supplied wholesale to the Huibei Electric Company, which then distributes it retail. The Daming Electric Company in the Fifth District of Nanhui County also ceased generating electricity in February of this year and contracted with Pudong Electric to purchase electricity for use by households in Zhoupu Town. Recently, the company plans to extend high-voltage transmission lines southward from Zhoupu Town, reaching the towns of Xiasha and Hangtou in the Sixth District. Electricity is expected to be available next month. Within the Sixth District, there are also towns such as Zhaojialou, Dujiahang, and Lujiahui, each with small power plants that are operating poorly. They are currently discussing cooperation methods with the company, aiming to switch to Pudong Electric for power supply. The original Nansha Electric Light Company in Nanhui County has recently expanded its capital and reorganized into the Nanhui Electric Company. They are also negotiating with Pudong Electric to purchase electricity, and an agreement has been reached. It is planned to extend a three-phase high-voltage 13,200-volt transmission line eastward from Hangtou Town, passing through Xinshichang Town and reaching the county seat directly, before extending south to Liuzaowan Town. It is reported that construction will be completed and electricity will be available within two months, providing day and night supply, which will be more convenient for users. General industry and commerce can also gradually see revitalization. The electricity can also be used for rural irrigation along the line, benefiting the local economy significantly.

French Concession Interpreter Extorts Money from Gu Songmao 132

Arrested After Discovery by the Detective Bureau

Captured After Returning from Escape

Huang Ruiting, a native of Ningbo, is currently thirty-three years old. In 1920, he joined the Traffic Department of the French Municipal Council as an interpreter. On September 10, 1933, Huang falsely claimed to Gu Songmao, a major rickshaw merchant, that the French Municipal Council's inspection of rickshaws was extremely strict. If he could be given a considerable sum of money, he could use his influence to provide special treatment and avoid harsh scrutiny. Gu agreed and paid him 670 yuan in foreign currency. Gu issued a check from the Jifeng Qianzhuang and delivered it to Huang at Gu's residence at No. 15 Hemin Lane, Xinjiang Road, Zhabei. Huang then affixed his seal and obtained the money from Jifeng. However, the matter was discovered by the Chief Inspectorate of the Detective Bureau, who ordered detectives to arrest him. However, Huang had already abandoned his post and fled. The Detective Bureau reported to the First Special District Court and issued Arrest Warrant No. 490. Recently, Huang, believing that the matter had passed, secretly returned to Shanghai and hid at No. 2, Lane 111, Oujia Road, Hongkou. This was discovered by the Chief Inspectorate, and Chief Detective Lu Liankui ordered Chinese Detective Liu Zhaokui, Detective Wu Hanzhang, Zhang Yunhong, and Western Detective Grover to arrest Huang at his home at 1:45 PM yesterday, and he was taken back to the Detective Bureau for detention. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Second Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. The Detective Bureau's lawyer, Qian Xunjiu, explained the background and charged Huang with extortion under Article 363 of the Criminal Code. He also stated that due to the urgency of the situation, the plaintiff, Gu Songmao, and witnesses Bao Zenghuang, Tao Bengong, Yin Zhifang, Liang Ruiting, and Hou Shao'an, had not been summoned and were unable to appear in court. Therefore, he requested that the case be rescheduled for hearing and submitted a photograph of the check as evidence to the court. Huang Ruiting argued that Gu Songmao had borrowed 2,500 yuan from him in June of the previous year, and that this 670 yuan was part of the repayment of his debt, not extortion. He also claimed that he had no authority to inspect vehicles, as that was the responsibility of Western supervisors. He hired lawyer Fan Gang to defend him. Judge Deng Baosun reviewed the evidence and ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody for a rescheduled hearing.

Zeng Mengpu Talks About Sai Jinhua 133

Mengpu Was Only Thirteen When Sai Married Hong Jun

"A Flower in a Sinful Sea" Was Written to Preserve Late Qing Anecdotes

Sai's Statements in Beijing Are Factually Incorrect

Recently, this newspaper published a dispatch from Beijing, recording the impressions and statements of the famous late Qing courtesan Sai Jinhua. The article mentioned "A Flower in a Sinful Sea," which was said to have changed Sai's name, and Sai Jinhua claimed that Zeng Pu wrote the book because of setbacks in love. This is truly an extraordinary and sensational anecdote in literary circles. Fortunately, both Ms. Sai and Mr. Zeng Pu are still alive, so it is not difficult to clarify the truth. Especially fortunate is that this reporter has a friendship with Mr. Zeng Pu despite the difference in age, so on a starry, moonlit, and chilly early winter night, I drove to Shanghai to visit him at his residence. Mr. Zeng Pu, whose courtesy name is Mengpu, is from Changshu, Jiangsu. In his youth, he was involved in officialdom and made many achievements in political circles. In recent years, he has retired to cultivate his garden, entertaining himself with flowers in his hometown's Xuxiao Garden in Changshu. In his spare time, he translates famous works of French and Russian literature to enjoy his later years. Every autumn and winter, he comes to Shanghai for a short stay to visit old friends and take care of miscellaneous affairs. This reporter was able to visit Mr. Zeng Pu during his short stay in Shanghai. Mr. Zeng is already sixty-three years old. His health is not very good, but his spirit is vigorous and his arguments are lively, and his enthusiasm is no less than that of a young person. Mr. Zeng has a long, thin face, a drooping beard, wears a blue coarse cloth gown, a white-topped melon-skin hat, and white shoes, mourning for his late mother. After a brief exchange of greetings, the reporter presented Mr. Zeng with the Shen Bao dispatch, asking for his criticism and thoughts on the matter. Mr. Zeng smiled and said, "This is probably because the reporter misunderstood Ms. Sai's words, or else it was intentionally fabricated. As far as I can tell, Ms. Sai would never say that I had a romantic relationship with her, because there is absolutely no such fact between us. In order to dispel misunderstandings from the outside world, I will briefly describe my relationship with Ms. Sai and the motivation for creating 'A Flower in a Sinful Sea.'"

(1) Sai Jinhua's Life and Relationship with Me

Sai Jinhua is originally from Yancheng. She claims to be from Suzhou. At the age of sixteen, she married Hong Jun, whose courtesy name is Wenqing, who was my father's sworn brother and also the teacher of my teacher. Therefore, we had the relationship of "Grand Teacher." Therefore, at that time, I often called Sai Jinhua "Little Grand Teacher's Wife." Sai married Hong Wenqing when she was sixteen years old, and I was only thirteen years old. How could I understand what love was? This is not just me saying it. There is documentary evidence. I currently have Mr. Yuan Shuangqiu's "Chang'an Banxi Poetry Collection." According to the collection, it was written in the year of Dinghai during the Guangxu reign. In this collection, before the poem "Sending Li Chunzhai, Observer, as Special Envoy to Japan," there is a poem titled "Sending Hong Wenqing, Academician, as Envoy to Russia and Germany," which is the poem in "A Flower in a Sinful Sea" that says, "Proclaim the imperial decree to the western sea, and present the heavenly book to the northern court." Wenqing originally went abroad as an envoy with Li Chunzhai and Xue Fucheng. According to this, the year of Wenqing's mission abroad was indeed Dinghai, and I was sixteen years old that year. Sai Jinhua's marriage to Wenqing was two or three years before the mission abroad, in the years of Jiashen or Yiyou during the Guangxu reign. The "Colorful Clouds Song" in the Fashan Poetry Collection states that Caiyun was sixteen years old when she married Wenqing, and I was only thirteen years old that year. Even if we push it down another year, I would be at most fourteen years old. How could there have been a relationship with Sai that involved recognizing and even falling in love with her? I first met Sai in Beijing. At that time, I was a secretary in the cabinet and often went in and out of Hong's residence, so I often saw her. At that time, Sai was very graceful and her eyes were bright. Even if she didn't speak, her eyes seemed to convey something, as if she were speaking. For example, when eating at the same table, if there were ten people, Sai could use her hands, eyes, and mouth to make all ten people feel very happy and satisfied. In other words, she would never neglect anyone. Sai was not a beauty with the appearance of the goddess Luo, but her face was upright. She was informal and didn't care about trivial matters, and she got acquainted with people very easily. When I met Sai, she was about twenty-seven or eight years old, wearing an embroidered dress and wearing the then-popular beard hairstyle. She had already returned from accompanying Hong on a mission to Western Europe. The Jiji collection of the Chang'an Banxi Poetry Collection was written in the year of Guihai. Among them, there is a poem titled "Between the Congling Snow Mountains, the Boundary Affairs Are Undetermined, Yang Yushang, the Attendant, Declares and Governs, and Enthusiastically Asks to Go, Jocularly Writing a Poem to Amuse Him." The so-called boundary affairs between the Congling Snow Mountains were due to the border issues that arose from Wenqing's Sino-Russian border map. Imperial Censor Yang was the one who impeached Wenqing and led the mission to survey the border. Later, Wenqing's affairs were also mediated by him. However, Wenqing soon died of depression because of this case, approximately in the autumn and winter of that year. Because the Hong family returned south in Jiawu, Sai Jinhua escaped from the ship at this time and broke away from the Hong family. She started a business in Shanghai under the name Cao Menglan. Suzhou gentry, because Sai lost the face of Suzhou people, Lu Runxiang and other gentry forced her to leave Shanghai. Therefore, Sai went north to Tianjin and again used the name Sai Jinhua. Sai had an affair with General Waldersee when she accompanied Hong on a mission to Germany. Therefore, when the Eight-Nation Alliance entered Beijing, Waldersee looked for her. Sai went to Beijing at Waldersee's invitation and still used the name Sai Jinhua. She accompanied Waldersee day and night, riding a horse and swaggering through the city, becoming extremely popular. The citizens of Beijing called her "Second Master Sai." When Waldersee returned to Germany, Sai was imprisoned in the Ministry of Justice for beating a maid to death. Her fellow prisoners included the revolutionary Shen XX (the protagonist of the Shanghai Subao case) and the old bureaucrat Su Yuanchun (who personally participated in the battle at Zhennanguan during the Sino-French War), known as the "Three Famous Prisoners." Later, she was sent by the Ministry of Justice to Suzhou, Changzhou, Yuanhe, and Wu County for a joint trial. Someone helped her from the inside, so she was released. She started a business again in Shanghai, still under the name Sai Jinhua. Later, she married Cao, a small clerk on the Jinpu Railway. Their relationship was very good until Cao died. She set up a business in Shanghai for the third time, next to the Grand Theater, still under the name Sai Jinhua. She met Congressman Wei, whom she married. She was about fifty years old at the time, around 1934. The last time I met Sai was at this time. Sai's spirit was still good, but she wore a lot of powder, and you could see that her skin was wrinkled. She liked to wear men's clothing. Regarding "A Flower in a Sinful Sea," Sai raised two protests: (1) She did not admit to being the daughter of a sedan chair carrier; (2) She did not admit to having a relationship with the captain during her voyage to Europe. She did not mention anything else. Sai did know foreign languages, at least she could speak English, French, and German. She did not know how to write. It is too much to say that she did not understand a single foreign language. Think about it, Sai had two close relationships with Waldersee, and the time was not just three or two days. How could she not understand a single word of German?

(2) The Motivation and Process of Creating "A Flower in a Sinful Sea"

Sai Jinhua said that I wrote "A Flower in a Sinful Sea" because of failures in love. I have already pointed out the fallacy in the above conversation. Now I will briefly describe my motivation for writing "A Flower in a Sinful Sea." In 1904, I recuperated in Shanghai due to illness and founded the Xiaoshuo Lin Publishing House in Shanghai. Jin Yi (courtesy name Songcen) from Suzhou submitted a manuscript entitled "A Flower in a Sinful Sea," consisting of six chapters. I revised it and wrote to him suggesting that we use Sai Jinhua as the warp and the anecdotes of the Qing Dynasty's court and the public during the past thirty years as the weft to compile a long novel. Jin Yi replied that he did not have such ambition, so he completely entrusted it to me. Therefore, the first chapter of the first edition of "A Flower in a Sinful Sea" was still written by Jin Yi. After I finished the first volume of "A Flower in a Sinful Sea," my father-in-law, Shen Meisun, saw it. Because the content was all about the anecdotes of seniors and friends, he was afraid that I would offend relatives and friends, so he hid it and did not allow it to be published. However, because this was the crystallization of my efforts, I was unwilling to bury it, so I took the opportunity to secretly print it. That was in 1906. In the preface to "The History of Bandits," Lin Qinnan revealed that "A Flower in a Sinful Sea" was written by Zeng Pu. For a time, many people contacted me to inquire about it. As for the content of "A Flower in a Sinful Sea," it is as Lin Qinnan said in the preface to "The Red Reef Painting Oar Record": "A Flower in a Sinful Sea is not a novel, but a history of thirty years." However, although there may be a considerable target when writing the novel, it is too ignorant of literary works to regard it as a true history and stick to it inch by inch.

A Young Woman Dies by Poisoning Due to a Letter from Her Husband 135

Seeking Funds to Return Home to Visit Her Mother

Replying Letter Was Reproachful by Her Husband

Zhang Meizhen, a woman from Hebei, is seventeen years old this year and married Hu Muxiu from Zhejiang as a concubine. Hu is a military man and currently serves as a staff officer in the Eighth Brigade Headquarters of the Third Division of the Army in Fujian. He left Ms. Zhang in Shanghai, living in the back room of a three-story building at No. 22 Hengqing Lane, Bellows Road, in the French Concession. All living expenses are remitted by Hu on a monthly basis. Recently, Meizhen received a letter that her mother in Yichang was seriously ill and urgently wanted to visit her, but she had no travel expenses. Therefore, she sent a letter to her husband, Hu Muxiu, requesting funds to visit her sick mother in Yichang. Unexpectedly, at around 1:00 PM on the 23rd, Meizhen received a reply letter from her husband sent by the post office. Upon opening the letter, not only was the request for money refused, but there were also words of reproach. Upon seeing the letter, Meizhen was filled with anger and sorrow, and burst into tears. After her roommates persuaded her to stop, she conceived the idea of suicide. She went out to buy sleeping pills and returned home, taking them while lying in bed waiting for death. At 7:00 PM, Zhang Mianren, a friend of her husband from Zhejiang living in the front room (who works at the Shanghai Art School on Caishi Road), discovered that she was calling out but unable to wake up. At 9:30 PM, he sent her to Baolong Hospital for emergency treatment. However, the poisoning was too deep and the treatment was ineffective. She died at noon yesterday. The hospital reported the suicide situation to the Xinzha Police Station, which in turn notified the French Police Station to send detective Maye to investigate the suicide. The body was taken to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch Forensic Center for examination. Because today is a Sunday holiday, they are waiting to report to the Second Special District Court tomorrow to send someone to examine the body. At the same time, the second landlord telegraphed the deceased's husband to handle the funeral arrangements.

Passenger on Jiangxin Steamer Attempts Suicide by Jumping into the River and Is Rescued 136

Crew Members Raise Money to Assist

The China Merchants Bureau's Yangtze River steamer Jiangxin, which sailed from Hankou to Shanghai this time, stopped at Jiujiang on the 22nd to load and unload passengers and cargo before setting sail again. Unexpectedly, no more than half a mile after the ship started, a passenger nearing 60 years old in the third-class cabin suddenly jumped into the river to commit suicide. Fortunately, the ship's tea boy and sailors spotted him and immediately reported to the captain to stop the ship. They quickly lowered a sampan and sent sailors to rescue him. Unexpectedly, the person who fell into the water was well-versed in swimming. Although he jumped into the water to commit suicide, he was also waiting for someone to help him. After being rescued from the water and brought onto the ship, the crew and the business director removed his wet clothes, provided him with food and medicinal wine, and asked him about the reasons for his suicide. According to the passenger, he was from Wuxue and was unable to borrow money from a friend in Wuhu due to difficult livelihood. He returned to Jiujiang, and now thinking that he had no way to make a living, he voluntarily took the steamer and jumped into the river to commit suicide. Whether this matter is true or not cannot be verified, but the crew members on the ship immediately raised more than 100 yuan to give to the passenger and sent him to Wuhu, which he wanted to go to, allowing him to go ashore.

Extortionist Comes to Collect Money 137

Wang Zongying Arrested on the Spot

On the morning of the 22nd of this month at 9:30 AM, the Cantonese Gan Zhu Pan family at No. 690 Broadway Road suddenly received a threatening letter from a bandit group demanding 500 yuan, otherwise they would take drastic measures. They also received a phone call instructing them to wrap the money in white paper and have someone wearing a blue cloth long gown send it to the entrance of the Xihua Road Post Office between 8:00 and 9:00 AM the next morning, where someone would come to meet them. The victim replied that the amount of money demanded was too large, and the result was reduced to 100 yuan. They immediately reported to the Huishan Police Station, which sent Chinese and Western detectives to secretly monitor the situation at the appointed time. They wrapped the money in paper to resemble 100 yuan, and the representative wearing the blue long gown waited for a long time at the agreed location, but no one came to talk. At around 11:00 AM the day before yesterday, Wang Zongying, a man from Jiangbei, 20 years old, suddenly came to the victim's door with a letter in his hand, lingering. He was spotted by the lane watchman, Wei Shu, who learned that he was asked by a small Ningbo person to deliver the letter to the Gan residence and bring back 100 yuan. He was arrested by Chinese detective Chen Baozhong of the police station, and the letter was taken to the police station for detention. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. The Municipal Council lawyer, Li Zhishan, stated the previous situation and requested an adjournment. He presented the two letters for inspection. When questioned, the defendant's confession was hesitant. Judge Xiao Xiexun ordered him to be detained and remanded in custody for further investigation.

Death by Playing with Electrical Wires 138

Mao Lingen Dies from Curiosity

Cao Amao, a resident of No. 4 Yaotun Bay, north of Xietu Road, who works as a craftsman in the Da Zhonghua Overshoe Factory, hired an electrician to install electric lights at his home the day before yesterday. At around 5:00 PM, Mao Lingen (27 years old), a friend of Cao from Haimen, came to Cao's house to talk to Cao. At that time, the wires had not yet been installed. Unexpectedly, Mao's curiosity arose, and he stepped forward and grabbed the wires with his hand. Unexpectedly, he was immediately electrocuted. By the time the electrician noticed and rushed to rescue him, it was too late, and he died immediately.
