Women's Corner

The Name and Reality of Gender Equality 209

— Zhang Zhimin

Since the Legislative Yuan passed Article 239 of the Criminal Law, which stipulates that a married woman who commits adultery shall be sentenced to imprisonment of not more than one year, and the adulterer shall be punished in the same way; but there is no provision for punishing a married man who commits adultery, the principle of gender equality in law is violated, which has caused fierce protests from women's circles in Beijing and Shanghai. This is indeed a good phenomenon. Regarding this issue, I remember Mr. Wang Chonghui, a Doctor of Law, made a statement: "A married woman who commits adultery is punished, while a married man who commits adultery is not. This is indeed based on physiological reasons. Old laws of various countries a hundred years ago were all like this, and even today there are three or four countries that still follow it, and our country is one of them."

Dr. Wang is a legal expert, so what he says must be based on evidence. According to him, the crime of adultery has historically been specifically designed to treat women, and it is based on physiological reasons (unfortunately, Dr. Wang did not specifically explain these physiological reasons). But he also said, "According to historical facts, in recent hundred years, this kind of law that treats men and women unequally has gradually decreased in the civilized countries of the world." What is the reason for this?

The reason for this is a long story, and it cannot be fundamentally discussed here. In short, it is because under the individual economic unit, women do not have an independent economic status and retreat into the family to become appendages of men (it is not without reason that they are commonly called dependents), male household slaves. Under such circumstances, women become men's property, with an absolute obligation to be chaste to men. Having illicit relations means that slaves are disloyal to their masters, so of course, they must be severely punished to stabilize the order of the family (beautifully named family happiness). The criminal punishment for adultery comes from this.

As for men, they are the head of the family, with the right to freely dispose of all property and dependents. To show their wealth and extravagance, they can not only take concubines and maids, but also seek pleasure in brothels. Society not only does not regard this behavior as inappropriate, but also admires it.

In recent hundred years, due to the development of machine industry and division of labor, machines can be used by women, and the family has been simplified, women have had the opportunity to make a living independently and have gradually escaped from household slavery. The call for women's liberation has arisen from this. At the same time, in the modern individual free competition economy, even within the scope of the family, men do not need redundant household slaves, but need a "good helpmeet" who can consciously take responsibility. Therefore, the criminal law punishing women for adultery has gradually been abolished in various industrial countries.

From a modern point of view, the relationship between the two sexes is entirely based on free will. There is freedom to marry and freedom to divorce, fundamentally breaking the concept of chastity; due to economic development and the resulting public social interaction between men and women, this concept of chastity cannot be maintained. But the fact has also proven that the fixed relationship between the two sexes, that is, the monogamous family system, does not completely fail to be established because of this. This is because, aside from the morality of chastity, there is also the necessity of common life between husband and wife, the necessity of cohabitation between the two sexes, and the conscious will as the basis for maintenance.

Based on the above views, demanding the abolition of the law punishing women for adultery is a clear and just proposition to eliminate the remnants of barbarism in history and to remove a layer of oppression from women. However, looking at the petition movement of representatives of women's organizations in Beijing and Shanghai, it seems that they do not intend to fundamentally remove the oppression of women. In their hearts, they still believe that it is necessary to use criminal punishment to punish women's adultery, but they feel that this unilateral provision hurts the face of gentry-class women, so they innovate and retain the "ill-treatment" suffered by women, and add the same "ill-treatment" to men in the form of retaliation. Such equality really shows that the personalities of husband and wife are not respected, which is somewhat not thorough.

I want to state that I am not advocating adultery. Adultery cannot be prohibited by law, nor can it be advocated by anyone. Generally speaking, the prevalence of adultery is due to economic reasons, the lack and imperfection of sexual life between men and women (such as many young men and women cannot marry due to livelihood problems, inappropriate marriages for the sake of wealth and power, the excessive concubines in wealthy families, discord between husband and wife, restrictions on livelihood and children, and even poor women who obtain invisible income through adultery with the consent of their husbands... etc.). All officially established couples know to restrain licentiousness and strive to maintain harmony between husband and wife and stability of family life from the needs of common life and the education of children. This is especially true among ordinary people, even among those whom the gentry class consider "ignorant women of the lower class." This is to ask the current "avant-garde" of women's liberation to relax.

Modern women, even in various industrial countries, have only achieved nominal equality in law, and are still far from actual equality. In the current economic system, although women have some opportunities to make a living, the opportunities for their careers are still fewer than those for men. Working women are even more particularly exploited by machines as weaker individuals. After marriage, women still fall into the status of household slaves or semi-slaves due to household services and the burden of giving birth to and raising children. Under this kind of actual inequality, if enthusiastic women's rights activists do not strive to improve women's status from these actual unequal situations and demand that the law give women special protection, and even deny or cover up this actual inequality, and only strive for legal equality on the surface, the result will be that women will still suffer. For the strong and the weak to sign an equal treaty while maintaining the status quo is to maintain the inferior position of the weak.

Even in the case of adultery, women in the current environment have less convenience and difficulty in committing adultery than men; men, with their superior economic and social status, can obtain more "tolerance" from the woman in their adultery, and it is feared that women will find it difficult to emulate! Moreover, for decades, customs and habits have regarded men's adultery as "nothing," while women's adultery is regarded as a heinous crime or a great shame! It is feared that these kinds of actual situations cannot be erased by the equality of half a law stipulating that men and women who commit adultery should be punished in the same way!

Legal Disputes and Others 210

— Fei

This time, the women's groups' legal dispute movement shows the different types of consciousness of the Chinese people. Regarding Article 239, it is said that 200 million men will have 300 million crimes, so they cannot be sentenced. Only women are specifically sentenced. The reason, needless to say, is that women are subordinate, private property, and must be chaste. After a dispute, famous jurists even nervously proclaimed: It is really impossible to sentence men. Because 30% of the men in your country take concubines, they will all become criminals. At least, it will be inconvenient to take mistresses in the future. However, this article has finally been submitted to the Legislative Yuan for reconsideration. However, before the event, a certain minister was deeply afraid that the "amendment of the original案" would be resubmitted, causing the old men to want to indulge but fear punishment, so he painstakingly came up with this opinion: the main point is to change the article to "a married man who commits adultery and destroys his family shall be punished." In other words, men can commit adultery as much as they want, as long as they are technically clever. If they don't cause trouble, it's fine. For example, secretly crossing Chencang, not openly occupying other people's wives and daughters, then that is considered legal behavior. These famous words and high views completely reflect the patriarchal, feudal, and capitalist residual consciousness in male-dominated society. Their painstaking efforts are nothing more than to make the wording plausible without hindering the licentious and indulgent behavior of men in the middle and upper classes, because the facts tell us that the general middle and lower households are struggling on the poverty and hunger line, who has the extra strength, money, and leisure to commit adultery and take concubines!

Secondly, there is the group of women's groups who are indignant and filled with righteous indignation in the legal dispute. They oppose the inequality of Article 239, and the principle is naturally correct, but may I ask, what does this ultimately contribute to the happiness between the two sexes? Article 1052 of the Civil Law stipulates that "one spouse may petition the court for divorce only if the other spouse has one of the following circumstances." Two of the ten provisions listed on the left are "committing adultery." The current "Criminal Procedure Law" restricts mutual accusations between husband and wife in order to maintain family harmony. That is, in the newly revised Criminal Law, Article 245 also stipulates that the crime in Article 239 "must be prosecuted upon complaint." Assuming that the result of the reconsideration is that men and women are punished equally, if we follow the litigation procedure, anyone who sues a husband for committing adultery must first petition the court for divorce, and only after the divorce can they sue him for the crime of adultery. Even if the law is enforced to punish the crime, what exactly does the woman gain? We must know that Article 256 of the current Criminal Law, which only punishes "married women" for committing adultery, is completely based on maintaining the family from the perspective of male power. This kind of article does not exist in a society with gender equality; it does not even exist in the more advanced capitalist countries in Europe and America. Now our women's groups are still bitterly demanding that men and women be punished equally, I don't know what for? If it is said that men will be even more unscrupulous if they are not legally restricted, then Articles 1056-57 of the Civil Law can originally be used for relief. If you are still afraid that men will use their economic power to do evil, then you may as well clearly stipulate that these two articles on compensation or alimony should be increased. Making them bear unbearable burdens and know what to worry about. Perhaps this can make them more disciplined. Wouldn't this be more practical?

There is another view that chastity is a remnant of feudal consciousness and should be eliminated. Legal documents do not contribute to the true equality between men and women. Article 239 of the Criminal Law is naturally undesirable, and it is not worth paying attention to whether it exists or is abolished. The fundamental thing is to seek improvement in the economic structure. With a good society, the two sexes can obtain the same happiness. This is quite worthy of deep thought (please refer to the Women's Special Issue No. 6 of the Great Evening News).

I believe that in today's Chinese society, since women have awakened to the status of human beings, they should strive for the expression of human beings. From this legal dispute, we can see that "the marriage system and family organization that have been passed down have fundamentally shaken in the face of the current era of ideological evolution and the impact of all kinds of trends" (Great Evening News editorial on the 17th). Then, the lesson of the facts: the road back to the family is no longer viable. The idea of being a virtuous mother and good wife cannot cope with modern life. Only by learning the knowledge and skills of being a human being can we strive hard and heroically for the equal human status of men and women!

As for Article 221 of the new Criminal Law, the victims are mostly households below the middle class. However, the degree of social attention it has attracted is far less than that of Article 239. This also shows the inertia of the law in protecting human rights and the general consciousness of society. However, natural and man-made disasters have led to widespread bankruptcy in rural areas and general poverty among citizens. In the human flesh market where girls are sold, which is the parental authority enjoyed by parents, I don't know how many girls under the age of fourteen are destroyed under money and bestial desires! Even if we win the restoration of the original text of the current Criminal Law (still changed to 16 years old), what will it contribute to the facts? Enthusiastic women's rights activists, please continue to work hard!

A Record of Visiting a Certain Girls' School 211

— Qian

This day was the date of a parents' meeting at a certain girls' school. Although a light drizzle fell from the sky and the ground was muddy and slippery, I happily clutched my dual-purpose blue cloth umbrella and followed Madam Landlord (whose daughter currently resides at the school), setting off for the school. After two difficult transfers and a walk along a winding gravel path, we finally arrived at our destination. Stepping through the small side gate, a glance around made me feel like the world was vastly different. In contrast to the narrow and filthy environment nearby, the school grounds featured towering Western-style buildings and sprawling green lawns. Wanting to find the Landlord's daughter, we began to stroll along the path, taking in the sights. We saw the kindergarten, the primary school, the kitchen, the dining hall, the washrooms, and the gymnasium. The construction and equipment of the buildings were indeed excellent, especially the piano room, of which there were more than twenty, almost making me think I had mistakenly entered a music academy.

Finally, we entered the secondary school section, which was where parents were being received that day. Here, the first things that caught my eye were two foreign women, their blonde hair combed smoothly and straight, and appearing to be in their late thirties. They stood under a horizontal banner reading "Welcome Parents" at the entrance, smiling broadly with their red lips, and constantly nodding their heads in greeting to the guests.

On the wall of the corridor facing the main entrance, two foot-square framed glass images were solemnly displayed, resembling ancestral tablets or spirit tablets. Upon closer inspection, I realized that the frames contained commendation certificates from the Education Bureau, praising the girls' school for its high pass rate in the entrance exams, surpassing other schools. Seeing this, I immediately thought of the lottery ticket shops at the intersection of Nanjing Road and Zhejiang Road, adorned with lights and decorations. Didn't the owners of these shops display on the counter at the entrance a golden statue of the God of Wealth, adorned with red paper and boldly inscribed with "Last Time's × Prize Won Here" as an advertisement to demonstrate the truth of their claims? The intention behind displaying these two commendation certificates at the girls' school was probably no different from that of the lottery shop owners. According to Madam Landlord, since acquiring these two commendation certificates, the number of students had suddenly increased, reaching six or seven hundred this semester, and the school was generally regarded as a model girls' school.

My original intention was only to observe whether the Westernization and intoxicating atmosphere within this Western-style school were any different from what I had personally experienced ten years ago. But now, this development compelled me to pay even closer attention to its curriculum and ideology. With this resolve, after finding the Landlord's daughter, I invited them to accompany me into a classroom for second-year junior high students. First, I flipped through their neat homework, English exercise books, but beyond thirty or forty new words, there was nothing of substance. Immediately afterwards, I picked up a Chinese composition book. Among the five or six essays, one was titled "Morning Assembly." As I was reading:

"During last week's morning assembly, students from a school for the blind and deaf came to sing hymns. This week's morning assembly featured students from the Fu'er Orphanage singing hymns," Madam Landlord suddenly flew into a rage, dragging her mother forcefully towards the classroom door. I looked up and, focusing my gaze, noticed three or four young girls with heavily rouged faces near the classroom entrance, arguing with the Landlord's daughter. They were implying that she (the Landlord's daughter), a primary school student, dared to bring guests to visit their secondary school section. Once I understood the situation, I strode out of the classroom.

Ascending the stairs, I impolitely walked into a classroom for second-year senior high students. This time, I began by flipping through the composition books. Among the many essays, one titled "On Women Governing the Home" particularly piqued my interest. Coincidentally, the first one I picked up contained the following two brilliant passages:

"Nora's departure caused a sensation, but she has already lost the sympathy of the world. If one Nora's departure has lost the sympathy of the world, the departure of thousands of Noras will inevitably be cursed and insulted by all under Heaven."

"The family is the manufacturing plant of good citizens. Without virtuous mothers in the home, how can the nation have good citizens?..."

Driven by curiosity, I disregarded the urgings of Madam Landlord and her daughter and continued to browse through several more composition books. Although none of them contained particularly original arguments, they all shared a common point: after introducing and expressing dissatisfaction with Hitler's new policies on women, they concluded:

"Those who have already entered the family need not go out again, while those who have not yet entered the family may be made to serve society..."

The true meaning here probably refers to the idea that married women should be content and dutiful, staying at home and being virtuous wives and good mothers, while unmarried women may as well go out and be vases for others.

In the large auditorium on the third floor, amidst many trendy young women (students) with heavily rouged faces and permed hair, we sat for a full four hours, only seeing half of the entertainment show. Before the show, the principal gave an opening address. The school had both male and female sections, and the principal was a brother and sister who took charge based on gender. Although it was the girls' school's parents' day, we only saw the female principal, in her late forties, wearing rouge and powder, permed hair, colorful clothes, a long scarlet necklace around her neck, and bracelets on her wrists, acting coy and coquettish, running back and forth. The speech and all the event management were handled entirely by her brother. The substitute speaker's speech was very short, the main point being that the purpose of this parents' meeting was to jointly conduct a new life movement between family and school!

The entertainment show had as many as twenty acts, some performed very well, but they were too Westernized. For example, when five- or six-year-old kindergarten students performed a facial expression song of "I See You," it was still exactly the same as when it was brought over from the West. Several small mouths kept singing I see you or You see me. Some of the female guests who came in behind me, while watching those innocent and lovely expressions, laughing until tears streamed down their faces, could only regretfully murmur to themselves: "It's so fun, but it's a pity we don't understand what they're singing." Another example was an English speech, which, although the speaker recited the speech fluently, those below the stage said it sounded like birds chirping. In addition, I also watched a historical performance of "Mother Meng Teaching Her Son." Combining all of this, it was no different from the education I received at a church-run girls' school ten years ago.

Disappointed, even though only half of the entertainment show had been performed, and the sky had become completely dark, I had no choice but to bid farewell. Just as I was walking out of the venue, I discovered five or six copies of "Hymns of Praise" in the book racks behind several seats. Asking the Landlord's daughter, she said that they were required to pray every morning and on Sundays. Coming downstairs, under the lights, I saw the following notice in the bulletin board outside the principal's office:

"In order to promote the balanced development of students in the three areas of education, each student must have a certain level of achievement in physical education, intellectual education, religious education, and social service each semester..."

Leaving the school gate, stepping back onto the muddy and winding gravel path, I couldn't help but put my hands together and chant "Amen, Model Girls' School!"

Mother 212

— Written by Tomita Michiko, Translated by Hong Guang

—Dedicated to Comrade H. of a certain spinning factory in Toyama—

We are almost finished with the cold dinner,

Before, we always ate hot dinners,

At this time, we would always smell the fragrance of the leftover vegetables.

When, Mother,

Will we be able to meet you?

Leaving you, these two children,

Your daughters, Mother,

In front of the beast-like roaring machines of this factory,

What kind of posture do they use to work for others?

——Alright, alright, I'm tired of hearing complaints!

Wrinkling your sun-blackened face as if about to cry,

Shaking your mud-stained hands as if warding off demons,

Grinding your blackened teeth,

Your face that immediately becomes angry,

The ugly wrinkles that anxiously appear on that face,

Mother, all of this,

How do your two daughters remember it?

——Sister, why doesn't our mother have a smile?

——Why isn't she as gentle as the mothers in plays and movies?

——Why can't we have a smiling, gentle mother?

My younger sister, still wearing my old cotton clothes,

Because she is a girl of seventeen,

After talking about clothes, Mother,

She talks to her sister about her own mother.

——Guangmei, don't mothers of tenant farmers in that place send their daughters out to work?

——In this kind of world, are the mothers of tenant farmers in that place gentle to their daughters?

——Why do tenant farmers have to send even their only daughters out to work?

——Why was Grandpa imprisoned in a dark jail for participating in the rent reduction movement?

——Why do we have to strike? And,

——Guangmei, why did that strike still fail us?

Her pale face fixed on me,

Eyes wide open, biting her lip,

Mother, because my younger sister Guangzi is also a trampled worker,

Also the daughter of a hungry tenant farmer's mother,

She listens to my words with enthusiasm,

Looking at me as if I were her enemy.

Although it is already dark,

Our poor tenant farmer's mother,

You are still dripping with snot,

Spreading fertilizer in the fields.

For understanding the overwork, your melancholy, your angry nature,

For the sake of not forgetting you,

For the sake of reaching the time when you begin to laugh from the bottom of your heart,

For the sake of reaching that bright time, Mother,

We must desperately work hard.

Although we are women,

For the sake of being able to laugh from the bottom of our hearts at that time,

For the sake of becoming true workers,

For the sake of being your hungry daughters.

The New "Obey Your Husband" Doctrine of the "Daughter's Classic" 213

— Cai Muhui

Judging from his method of arrangement, the editor of the "Daughter's Classic" seems to have attempted to encompass all women's issues in the script. I just don't know why the lives of the eight or nine female protagonists he describes all seem to be manipulated by relations between the sexes, and their destinies are entirely controlled by sexual relations. Is it possible that women's abilities will always be as insignificant as Sun Wukong, while the supernatural power of relations between the sexes is as vast as that of the Buddha, so that no matter how many somersaults Sun Wukong performs, he can never escape the Buddha's palm?

I remember that twenty years ago, my grandmother often said with a sigh: A woman's fate is like a fallen flower. If it falls into a clear goldfish pond, she is extremely fortunate. If it falls into a stinking open-air manure pit, she is unlucky for life. Whether she falls well or badly, however, is not up to the woman to decide. The Old Man Under the Moon arranges it as he pleases. At that time, I already had a "so-so" amount of awareness of resisting the old moral code, so I said to my grandmother: I will definitely not be a fallen flower, but will be like a butterfly, flying freely to the east and flying to the west. My grandmother therefore cited the past events of women in her hometown one by one, and also talked about the various misfortunes of her four aunts, trying to convince me. Unfortunately, as she spoke, my grandmother's throat seemed to suddenly suffer from a cold and could not make much sound, and tears, like prayer beads with a broken string, fell one by one onto her clothes.

My grandmother's words were excusable. In her time, women still did not have a recognized social status. Unless they dared to play the role of the female protagonist who "poured water before the horse," they had no choice but to accept their fate and follow the chicken if they married a chicken, and follow the dog if they married a dog. They had no way to create their own destinies on their own. But now, the number of women who, like men, rack their brains, shed their own blood and sweat, and struggle and strive in the industrial, commercial, and cultural circles is already considerable. They are all able to grasp their own destiny and are unwilling to be like fallen flowers with no future, but it is only a mutual and relative influence after all, and they do not make contributions. It is just a pity that the editor of the Daughter's Classic only depicts a false feminist who absolutely contradicts herself in word and deed and is willing to be a man's gramophone, and a female shop assistant who has been subjected to all kinds of coercion and enticement by the opposite sex. Apart from this, he has not mentioned any women who live professional lives and are not controlled by sexual relations. This is a film that was compiled and performed in 1934. How could it represent my long-deceased grandmother's view of life? Promoting the "New Obey Your Husband" doctrine?

Oh, I remember now. When I was only nine years old, because I was unwilling to sit quietly at home, my grandmother forced me to read a Daughter's Classic. In that book, there were many unbearable lessons. Perhaps the editor of this 1934 "Daughter's Classic" wanted to fulfill his mission of teaching women who were unwilling to follow the old moral code? It is just a pity that the new daughters of today already have facts leading them to see a world outside of the relations between the sexes, and are no longer willing to believe in the "obey your husband" doctrine, even if it is a very new and trendy "New Obey Your Husband" doctrine.

Hasn't that Daughter's Classic, which women and mothers in our grandmothers' time all had to listen to, already disappeared invisibly? I think no one will believe the teachings of this new "Daughter's Classic," which is old wine in new bottles, right?

Random Thoughts 214

— Shuiyin

Some women seem willing to be looked at by others forever and do not want to raise their heads and strive for a little social status, always dressing themselves up in gaudy colors. This is something that advanced women engaged in the women's movement should be ashamed of.

Advanced women engaged in the women's movement should not only focus on women in the intellectual class, but should broaden their horizons and see the other corner of society, working women, rural women, and the petty bourgeoisie.

Rouge and lipstick do not seem very good, it is best not to use them; the white powder of the past and the red paint of the present, red and white are really the same.

Women's struggle for social status, I can say with certainty: "It is definitely not on the outside, but on the inside." May I ask, what can someone with no learning or talent do? Even if there is an opportunity, there is no way to do it.

The most suitable profession for women is elementary school teacher. In the United States, women account for more than 80% of elementary school teachers; but modern Chinese women do not want to be elementary school teachers, and seem to hate this profession the most, thinking it is unworthy, which is wrong.

Chinese women have not yet earned a little social status, female socialites are still very difficult to find, and there are not many women in publications about women who are willing to speak and do things; this is something that people engaged in the women's movement should be concerned about.

Think of a way to prevent women from hiding in their families.

Finance 215

Large Investors Vigorously Purchase, Guangdong Merchants Cover Short Positions, Gold Prices Continue to Soar

—Resulting in a Further Increase of 9.6 Yuan—

The gold market has been firm for consecutive days. Yesterday's market continued its strong upward trend. Amidst constant rumors, buyers were happy to be active. Large investors repeatedly purchased vigorously, and Guangdong merchants also entered the market to cover their short positions. The market situation remained persistently firm. Even with the efforts of the Price Stabilization Committee to lower prices by reducing the balance tax by half a percentage point, it did not affect the overall situation. In the morning, overseas silver markets saw British prices flat and American prices rising. The forward silver price in Montreux narrowed by 4.5%. Exchange rates were flat. London pure gold rose by two pence. When off-exchange pre-market trading opened, it immediately retreated to 1006.7 yuan. Eager buyers quickly emerged, and prices were immediately pulled up. The Central Bank's official listing showed both British and American prices flat. The customs gold unit rose by 0.03 yuan. The standard price for gold was 1003.3 yuan. Market sentiment was very bullish, and the morning opened with high prices. Although there was a slight dip after the opening, buying interest was strong. The foreign exchange market was also tight, rising beyond the 10-yuan mark. Banks were still absorbing supply and had positions to manage. The HSBC official listing revealed a decrease of 0.125 for British currency and 0.3125 for American currency. Large investors continued to enter the market, leading to further price increases. However, because banks were still willing to sell, prices gradually retreated. The silver balance tax was announced, only levied at 6.25%, half a percentage point lower than before. This was an unexpected move by the Price Stabilization Committee to suppress the market. Prices weakened for a time, retreating below the 10-yuan mark. However, large investors, considering the low balance tax, believed that silver would flow out in large quantities, leading to a credit crunch. The government would inevitably try to stop this. Therefore, although market sentiment was fatigued, it was not alarmed. Under the vigorous buying by large investors, prices gradually turned bullish again. In addition, banks only had recent-term selling appetite, and the forward exchange market tightened. Once the buying trend started, the upward momentum was revived. Yuan Mao Yong, with extremely aggressive buying, swept the market. At the same time, the Guangdong merchants also covered their short positions through him, pushing prices beyond the 20-yuan mark. Sellers took advantage of the high prices. At the same time, rumors spread that a certain party was coming to suppress prices. Buying interest faded at this point, retreating below the 20-yuan mark, and downstream transactions were also quick. However, market sentiment was already bullish, and even after the decline, there was still upward momentum. However, the selling interest of large investors revived, and the situation suddenly became one of oversupply, leading to another decline. However, prices were pulled up at the noon closing. After the closing, the Guangdong merchants continued to buy, and the underlying trend remained bullish. The half-day market situation was extremely volatile. This was also expected. The volume of open positions remained at around 26,000. The half-day market situation is recorded below.

The morning opening was 1009 yuan, an increase of 2.2 yuan compared to the previous closing. Heng Yu, Fu Yu, Qing Yu, and Fu Xing Yong sold off, retreating to 7 yuan. Zheng Chang, Zhao Feng, Chang Da, Fa Yong, Fu Yu, and others came in to buy, rising to 12 yuan. Fu Xing Yong supplied contracts, lowering to 1009.8 yuan. Market sentiment remained bullish. Yuan Yi Xiang, He Xiang, Da Fa Yong, and Shang Jin rose again to 13 yuan. Hua Bi quoted US dollars for December at 25. Fu Xing Yong and Heng Yu sold and then bought, rising from 0.5 yuan to 3.5 yuan. Mai Jia Li quoted shillings for February at 8125. Qing Yu, Zhao Feng Chang, Yu Xin Xiang sold contracts, falling to 1 yuan. Anticipating that the HSBC official listing would show a decrease of 0.125 for British currency and 0.3125 for American currency, Tian Feng Yong, Shen Kang, Yuan Mao Yong, Hui Xiang, Fu Xing Yong, Heng Yu, and Zheng Chang vigorously bought, rising to 16 yuan. Yi Feng Yong, Da Fa Yong, Qing Yu, Fu Xing Yong, Heng Yu, Fu Yu, Yi Cheng, Tian Feng, Hong Xing, Heng Xing Yuan sold contracts, gradually falling to within 1 yuan. Banks still had a selling appetite. Wan Xing, Zheng Chang, Da De Cheng, Yuan Mao Yong, Hui Xiang, and Shang Na gradually rose to above 3 yuan. The silver balance tax was announced, retreating to 6.25%. British gold was calculated at 1 shilling 5 pence 6875, half a percentage point lower than before. Market sentiment weakened as a result. Tong Tai Chang, Da Fa Yong, Heng Yu, Yuan Mao Yong, Zhao Feng Chang, and others supplied contracts, retreating to 1009.7 yuan. The Dalian merchants bought contracts on the dip, rising to 11.8 yuan. Retail investors continued to supply, and Da De Cheng and others also sold slightly, falling again to 1009.7 yuan. Heng Xing, Heng Tai, Dalian merchants, Da De Cheng, and others jointly bought, gradually rising back to 14.3 yuan. Shun Mao, Zhao Feng Chang, and Yi Cheng took advantage of the high prices to supply contracts, falling back to 1.5 yuan. Helplessly, banks only had recent-term selling appetite, and the forward exchange market remained tight. Heng Yu, Fu Yu, Fu Xing Yong, and Heng Xing all bought, rising to 6.5 yuan. Da Fa Yong sold and then bought, and retail investors rushed to cover. Wan Xing, Heng Yu, Yuan Mao Yong, Qian Chang Xiang, Qing Yu, and others also bought. The buying trend became even stronger. After entering, Yuan Mao Yong's buying interest was extremely strong, and sellers were helpless, rising to 21 yuan. Da De Cheng, Heng Yu, Yi Cheng, and Yi Feng Yong sold, retreating to 19.5 yuan. Silver Dollars Shipped to Hong Kong for Transfer Abroad

Silver exports have been affected by customs regulations, leading to repeated changes in transit destinations. Initially, due to increased customs duties, silver was shipped to various parts of South China and then exported abroad. Now, due to the Ministry of Finance's order requiring passports for the circulation of silver dollars within the country, silver traders face even greater difficulties. It is reported that exporting silver abroad, after paying taxes, is still profitable. Therefore, in the past three days, over 1.2 million silver dollars have been shipped to Hong Kong for re-export.

Securities 216

Public Bonds Unexpectedly Face a Short Squeeze on the Last Day of This Month

Various Items Fall by 0.1 to Over 1 Yuan

Yesterday, the Chinese Merchant Securities Exchange saw a generally peaceful last day for this month's futures contracts. However, in the last five minutes, there was some mutual squeeze, with the trend leaning towards a short squeeze. This was because the market had been experiencing short squeezes for several months, leading to a widespread belief that the market might switch to a long squeeze. Long positions held on for a long time, and only on the last day were they forced to liquidate, resulting in another short squeeze. Although interbank lending rates decreased by 0.02 yuan, credit conditions became increasingly tight. The future of interbank lending rates was not expected to decline. There were rumors in the market that the future was not promising. Yesterday's trading saw a stable opening in the morning, with most items slightly up by 0.1 to 0.2 yuan, mainly due to retail investors buying in. In the second round of trading, numbers 11, 16, and 48 sold off uniformly, causing prices to retreat by 0.2 to 0.3 yuan. The prices for this month's contracts were the lowest, mostly due to long positions rolling over. In the afternoon, rumors suddenly arose, causing market sentiment to become nervous. Number 50 also sold off, intensifying the decline by another 0.3 to 0.4 yuan. The closing saw the most significant short squeeze on demobilization contracts, with this month's contracts falling by almost 1 yuan at its steepest, the most intense squeeze in recent days. Other items saw smaller declines. The future trend was not expected to rebound. The fact that there were still short positions covering their positions prevented an even steeper decline. The resulting price declines were uneven, ranging from 0.1 to 0.2 yuan to over 1 yuan. The contract squeeze was alarming. The total trading volume was approximately 25 million yuan. Grains 218

Flour Market Sees Sudden Surge Amidst Rumors of Increased Tax on Foreign Wheat

Yesterday, the flour market initially opened with stable to slightly higher prices in the morning. The pricing of foreign wheat in Chicago showed only minor fluctuations of around 1/4, while Canadian wheat fell by about 2 jiao. Consequently, market sentiment remained initially calm at the opening. However, due to observations from both industry insiders and outsiders, and influenced by the recent surge in soybean oil prices following tariff increases, concerns arose that import duties on foreign wheat might also increase. Additionally, rising gold prices added to the anxiety, leading to increased buying activity and a gradual rise in market prices, approximately 2 fen higher than the previous day. In the afternoon, market conditions further intensified, fueled by rumors of impending tax increases on foreign wheat. This triggered short covering and aggressive buying, causing a dramatic surge in prices. However, actual sales remained sluggish. Given the current famine in the country and the importance of flour as a staple food, some believe the rumors may not be entirely credible. As a result, the price for the current month rose by 7 fen and 2.5 li, while prices for December and January rose by 6.5 fen, February by 7 fen, March by 8 fen, and April by 7 fen.

Yesterday, the wheat market maintained relative stability in the morning. The pricing of foreign wheat showed only minor fluctuations of around 1/4 in Chicago and roughly 2 jiao in Canada. At the opening, prices for the current month saw only slight variations due to the approaching settlement date, with limited transactions. Trading in distant months remained quiet, with few sellers and active buyers. Consequently, opening prices were 3 to 4 fen higher. In the afternoon, positive activity in the flour market and rumors of increased taxes on foreign wheat fueled buying interest and drove prices higher. This unexpected rumor broke the prolonged market stagnation. As a result, the price for the current month rose by 9 fen, December by 8 fen, January by 1 jiao and 1 fen, February by 1 jiao and 1 fen, and March by 1 jiao and 3 fen. The current wheat market is showing increased activity, but factories are hesitant to purchase. It is reported that Shandong wheat is being quoted at 3 yuan 8 jiao 5 fen, and second-grade wheat at 8 jiao 2 fen.

The Chicago wheat market has been influenced by unconfirmed reports of French wheat imports, suggesting potential selling activities there. Rumors indicate continued orders for corn imports, and the government supposedly disapproves of rising grain prices. It is widely believed that a powerful inflationary group has been formed among the incoming members of parliament, which is gaining attention.

Market Prices 221

Shen Bao Local Supplement Amateur Weekly

Amateur Musings

Occupation and Intelligence 222

— Pheasant Feather

There are five kinds of intelligence: Mechanical, Abstract, Social, Aesthetic, and Moral. Mechanical intelligence refers to the ability to repair broken watches, fix broken things, and so on. People with this kind of intelligence easily approach and understand machines without special training. Abstract intelligence is entirely different. People with this kind of intelligence are particularly interested in abstract things and show their abilities in these areas. Students who do well in all school subjects, have a strong desire for knowledge, and are good at writing are those with this kind of abstract intelligence. There is also a type of student who is not good at academics or sports, but has a special talent: socializing. They can quickly get to know strangers and get everyone to recognize them and be willing to elect them as chairman or representative. We say that this kind of person is rich in social intelligence. Aesthetic intelligence is easy to understand, referring to the ability to distinguish and judge. People with this kind of intelligence can easily see the beauty or ugliness of something, or the goodness or badness of a thing. As for moral intelligence, it is the kind of intelligence that avoids making mistakes in morality or law. People with this kind of intelligence know how to avoid doing bad things, can "enter a country and inquire about its customs," and are generally more well-rounded in their behavior.

These five kinds of intelligence are all very important. Most people only have one or two of them. Those who have three or four are not ordinary, and those who have all five are even more remarkable.

These kinds of intelligence are closely related to our career choices and professions. Whether a profession is suitable for us depends on whether we have the ability and interest to engage in it. Only with these conditions can we choose a career that we can "handle with ease and joy," "achieve twice the result with half the effort," and ultimately succeed. That is, if our intelligence is close to a certain profession, and we choose that profession accordingly, the natural result will be a high degree of achievement in that profession. Otherwise, it is like a "blind man riding a blind horse." Not knowing how to choose the most suitable profession and just stumbling around randomly will rarely lead to failure.

But how can we know if we have a certain kind of intelligence? This can be seen from our school grades and our special interest in something. If we love mathematics and physics and have excellent results in these areas, then undoubtedly we have this talent and need to develop it.

Page 20

; if we are interested in mechanical things in any setting and want to explore the inner secrets of machines anytime, anywhere, like the newsboy Edison, then undoubtedly we also have this talent and need to develop it. Thus, the path of an inventor is arranged before us. Also, if we are not interested in machines or schoolwork, but show a special talent for speech, debate, and social interaction, then we must not ignore this talent. Schools may not necessarily promote these, and society may not necessarily encourage these, but these are still important and require our close attention. This is a necessary ability to serve society. The most powerful people in the world often have this kind of intelligence. The people who are most prominent on the world political stage or the most successful in their careers are also mostly people with this kind of intelligence. "Bookworms" are only fit to be their secretaries, and even inventors are often their puppets.

Chinese education does not seem to pay much attention to developing students' social intelligence, but only focuses on developing their abstract and mechanical intelligence. Chinese society in general shares the same view. For the sake of future success in the workplace, and so that those in the workforce can encounter fewer difficulties in their professions, I believe that social intelligence really needs attention. This is not only a standard for choosing a career, but also a factor that makes professional life enjoyable.

Here, I do not want to make a detailed explanation for abstract, aesthetic, and moral intelligence. But in general, people with abstract intelligence are best suited for writing, people with aesthetic intelligence are best suited for artistic things, and people with moral intelligence are best suited for reforming society. These are just views on how these kinds of intelligence affect career choices. In reality, these kinds of intelligence are also important for people who already have a profession. Developing these kinds of intelligence, or one or two of them, is a way for professionals to make their careers successful. We can say that in the journey of life, none of these kinds of intelligence can be dispensed with, but some people need more or less of them.

Overseas Correspondence Outline

— (Correspondence from Paris, France)

The Scenery of Versailles 223

— Spring Rain

Everyone knows that Versailles is a place as old and famous as the French capital, Paris. Indeed, it is in the suburbs of Paris, and very close to the suburbs. From Paris to there, it takes at most half an hour by train, so it could originally be discussed under the name of Greater Paris. However, if so, it would be wronged, because its fame has its own independent historical relics. This is not only because there is a majestic palace, great fountains, and a forest of towering trees, making it a scenic spot in France that is admired by tourists, but also historically, because it has become a solid fortress for nobles, princes, and all old authorities. Although this fortress can no longer protect them now, that is another question. In fact, everyone knows that in 1871 it had played a great role in defending the authorities of the time, because they used it as a strong wall for final self-defense and counterattack, and thus turned defeat into victory and finally defeated the common people of Paris. Versailles, it also left its immortal name for the first time. Of course, if we still want to talk about its historical relics, then the settlement of the 1914 Great War was also the signing of the treaty in Versailles, so its fame has spread all over the world even in recent times.

"Hey! Look! That section, although not very big, is also very majestic, is the earth mound of Versailles! That great, magnificent, ancient and healthy building, not very high or very short, unfolded a large area from the green shade, shining its golden yellow in the crystal white sunlight, is the Palace of Versailles!", a friend who had been there pointed out to me in the car, and told me with a tone of praise and surprise.

A few minutes later, the car stopped like a dead snake. Tourists carrying suitcases, wine bottles, bread, and fruits poured out of the car like water from a breached dam, and surged up the lazy hillside like a tide on the beach, and then slowly dispersed like splashes of waves, hiding in the forest of Versailles and the imperial palace. This is one of the French's usual ways of enjoying themselves, of course, most of them can only do so on holidays.

We, who are exhausted after a week of work, have of course learned this foreign habit, and we actually went to Versailles in the same way, and even ran up the hillside in one breath. We first paid homage to the Emperor's Palace. In this long-famous imperial palace, all the eaves, walls, and ceilings are carved with ancient, strong, complex, and beautiful patterns; the golden-yellow jacaranda wooden floor makes it difficult for us, the commoners who have never been called ministers and servants, to walk, and if we are not careful, we will slip and fall. Fortunately, I held the vigilant attitude of being afraid of being laughed at by foreign friends, and after "visiting it all over," I did not fall once. The Palace of Versailles is now a large museum. French paintings from the Middle Ages to the present are countless. Animals and plants, mineral specimens, gems and jade, relics of ancient humans: stone knives, stone axes, stone arrows, all human inventions in history: ancient knives, ancient swords, and even ancient embroidery and ancient textiles, are all available like other museums. But it can also make us Chinese feel a sense of melancholy in the midst of joy, that is, there are also displayed small feet embroidery shoes, opium pipes, and so on. Of course, this kind of special customs and habits, each nation has shown some ridiculous quirks at certain stages of development, but after French tourists see it, a cold and mocking attitude makes you feel a little sad! In the hall of Versailles, the signature pen of the last peace treaty, as well as the chairs of the adults and gentlemen, are displayed, which is a proud memorial of the Allied Powers, but also a bloody memorial of the 20 million innocent victims of the last war, the pen is inserted in their flesh and blood!

Below the imperial palace, there is a huge semicircular fountain, divided into several levels of size. Each level of the pond bank, pond heart, and bank feet has water pipes. And the pond bank and pond heart are sculpted with countless nude beauties and beasts, holding flowers, bottles, and plates on their heads in their hands, and spraying straight and horizontal water from the mouths of those animals, like many silver guns and white swords interlaced and chiseled. In the center are several larger nude female statues, with several jets of water shooting from this place in the high sky above their heads, all converging there and falling down, snowflakes and rain falling on their bodies. There are also several semi-flat jets of water that are aimed at their ×× parts. Several main trunks of the fountain are shooting straight upwards, as high as ten feet or so; the water lines falling from the top are like drooping ears of wheat, and the top is also like silver flowers in full bloom. The white light shines in all directions, and the beautiful and dazzling fountain of Versailles is truly worthy of being the world-famous fountain.

On the hillside of Versailles, there is a man-made waterfall, which also uses high-pressure water source as a spring. The artificial chute of a waterfall is from several feet to several feet wide, built into countless stone steps. Under the stone steps, various colored electric lights are installed, which are opened at night, and the thin water flows over them, showing a colorful beauty, which makes people want to taste it. The opportunity to open this kind of waterfall is even less than that of the fountain, and it is rare to appreciate it.

We once swam in the Versailles forest in the hot summer weather. The area of this forest is very large, and the tallest trees are cultivated. Of course, there are cypresses, vine trees, etc. The shade is so dense that even under the strong sunlight of midsummer, you can only find a gap in the thin foliage to peek at the tourists. The tender green grass and the towering leaves in the sky compete for the green and emerald, and compete for the refreshing and fragrant air, not only making people forget the heat of the midsummer in their arms, but also the slight cool breeze, which has the image of the season returning to spring, and intoxicating the tourists. In the forest, there are paved roads crisscrossing, and the branches on both sides are cut so that the bottom is wide and the top is narrow, becoming a natural bridge canopy, blocking the sky at the top, making you unable to see birds flying or clouds passing. After the drizzle, the asphalt road was originally spotless, and at this time it was slippery and shiny, even brighter than the oily face of old-fashioned Chinese women. In this forest, there are often millions of tourists drunk and full, and young men and women also take this opportunity to be intoxicated in the sea of natural and sexual love, they hug and sleep on the shaded grass, which is not considered strange by the French. The scenery of Versailles is the ultimate beauty of nature, and on this point, it does not live up to its world-renowned history, but this can only become a paradise for the upper classes of France to be drunk and full all day long, and most people can only try it occasionally.

Book Spring

Review of "Collection of Prejudices" 225

— A Compilation

——Published by Zhengzhong Bookstore, priced at six jiao——

Anyone who has read Mr. Liang Shiqiu's articles knows that he has a fixed system of literary theory. No matter the occasion, as long as literary issues are discussed, he always starts from the viewpoint that "literature originates from human nature, is based on human nature, and ends in life" (see Liang's "Romantic and Classical": Crescent Edition) to explain all literary phenomena. At the same time, under this viewpoint, he also has a fixed "prejudice," namely, that he believes "human nature is permanent, universal, fixed, without limitations or distinctions of time and space" (see Liang's "Literary Discipline"). Therefore, in his view, literature, as a "product of human nature," is the same in ancient and modern times, in China and abroad, permanently unchanging, and without distinction between old and new.

Mr. Liang's recently published "Collection of Prejudices," although composed of thirty-one articles on literary theory of varying lengths, still expresses his consistent literary views under his inherent "prejudice." This consistent view is, of course: "The essence of literature is the description of human nature" (see "Human Nature and Class Nature"). "Great literature is based on fixed, universal human nature, and thoughts flowing from the depths of the human heart are good literature. What is rare in literature is being true to human nature. As for how it relates to the trends of the times, whether it is influenced by the times or influences the times, whether it aligns with revolutionary theory or is constrained by traditional thought, it is irrelevant and does not affect the value of literature. Because human nature is the only standard for measuring literature" (see "Literature and Revolution"). "Human nature is unchanging. Emotions are neither new nor old. Literature is permanent" (see "The Permanence of Literature"). Mr. Liang can truly be called a literary critic who is consistent and forever "true to human nature."

However, do you believe that the lives, personalities, thoughts, and emotions of people in ancient times are exactly the same as those of modern people? Can you say that the parallel prose of the Wei and Jin Dynasties, the poetry of the Tang Dynasty, the Yuan Dynasty opera, the popular novels of the Ming and Qing Dynasties, and the vernacular literature after the "May Fourth" Movement are the same? If not, then the so-called "fixed, universal human nature," and "permanently unchanging literature" exist only in Mr. Liang's "prejudice" and cannot be found in the human world at all.

At the same time, Mr. Liang himself also said: "What kind of era produces what kind of literature, what kind of person writes what kind of work, this is absolutely correct" (see "On Modern Literature"). "Chinese traditional opera has a long history, is deeply rooted in the folk, and is still deeply ingrained today... Before Chinese society as a whole accepts Western culture, traditional opera will always exist; in other words, as long as China's ancient social traditions are preserved, traditional opera can undoubtedly prolong its life. At present, traditional opera still has its large audience, while emerging spoken drama is only weakly supported by a very small number of intellectuals" (ibid.). If literature is permanently unchanging, without distinction between old and new, then how can we explain the statement "What kind of era produces what kind of literature"? What should be the explanation of terms such as "traditional opera" and "emerging spoken drama"? Furthermore, "As long as China's ancient social traditions are preserved, traditional opera can undoubtedly prolong its life"; if we say it the other way around, it would be: "Once China's ancient social traditions die, the life of traditional opera will immediately be cut off." But this shows a truth: literature is a product of society and develops with the development of society; Chinese traditional opera is dependent on Chinese old society and survives or dies with the old society. In this case, the theory that literature is the same in ancient and modern times and is permanently unchanging is truly an incomprehensible "prejudice"!

However, Mr. Liang also says from another perspective: "Writers do not express the spirit of the times, but the times do reflect the spirit of writers" ("Literature and Revolution"). If we put this together with his view that literature has nothing to do with the times and is permanently unchanging, and then add his statement "What kind of era produces what kind of literature," then you will not know what trick Mr. Liang is playing. Because anyone can see that these three opinions are mutually contradictory, but Mr. Liang clings to these three mutually contradictory opinions and believes that they are all correct. Thus, can you say where Mr. Liang's correctness lies?

However, Mr. Liang says that "the times reflect the spirit of writers" for another purpose. Because he is superstitious about genius, believing that everything in the human world is created by geniuses, he has to use this as the basis of his theory. Listen to what he says—"All civilization is created by a very few geniuses. Science, art, literature, religion, philosophy, writing, as well as political thought and social systems, are all produced by a small number of people with extraordinary intelligence and talent." According to this statement, if there were no geniuses, no "small number of people with extraordinary intelligence and talent," then perhaps human society would not exist. Genius, truly the god-like person who creates everything!

Why can genius create everything? In Mr. Liang's view, of course, it is because they are different from the crowd, because they are especially smart and especially talented. But why are geniuses different from the crowd? Perhaps we can only say that they are "Heaven's chosen ones." But if a genius is born into the world, and no one makes food, clothes, or builds houses for them, and there is nothing for them to study, and they live in absolute solitude, then can they create anything? If so, then they would truly be a god-like person!

Genius creates everything, needless to say, this is also a "prejudice."

Mr. Liang opposes the theory of "art for art's sake" because this theory is not "serious"; but he wants to maintain the "independence" of literature, opposes the combination of science and literature, and opposes using scientific methods to study literature. At the same time, he firmly says: "Anyone who looks for other methods outside the scope of art and literature to use as a universal key to explain all literature is probably doomed to fail, although their failure is sometimes glorious" ("On the Third Kind of Person"). Look, isn't this the theory of "art for art's sake"?

Enough, there are too many "prejudices" in "Collection of Prejudices" to finish talking about, let's stop here.

Literary Works

Hunter's Leisure 226

— Zhou Leshan

Brigadier General Zhang had made great achievements in battle, so the young women in Place H respected him more than other heroes of the same age. When he was young, he was passionately in love with Ping. He believed that she was the most beautiful and lovely woman in Place H. Methodically, Brigadier General Zhang spent all his fortune to host banquets for her, hoping to win her love. But this woman already had a husband, so she didn't care about him at all.

With such a high degree of extravagance, Brigadier General Zhang quickly became impoverished and was forced to move to a small village to live. But he still kept a falcon he loved, one that could not be bought anywhere else. Now, his only remaining happiness was this falcon, on the other hand, working to support himself.

Soon Ping's husband died of illness. When the one-year mourning period expired, Ping moved to another environment, which happened to be very close to Brigadier General Zhang's village. Now, Ping's son had become a skilled hunter, and when he saw Brigadier General Zhang's lovely falcon, he wanted to get it very much. But he couldn't think of a way to get it, he knew how much the owner of this falcon loved it. Finally, the child fell ill. His mother loved her only son extremely, she took care of him, begging him to say what he wanted in this world. He told his mother that he wanted Brigadier General Zhang's falcon, and if he couldn't get it, he would have no hope of living.

Loving her son so much, Ping tried to think of a way to satisfy him. She recalled Brigadier General Zhang when he was rich, how he often tried all sorts of methods to make her happy. She felt she couldn't immediately go and talk to him. As a result, she allowed her son to get this falcon, so she went to visit Brigadier General Zhang with a girlfriend.

It happened that this day was not suitable for letting the falcon out to forage for food, so Brigadier General Zhang was in his garden. When Ping called him, he was surprised and speechless, and rushed out to welcome her.

"Brigadier General Zhang," she said, "I am here to repay all the misfortune you suffered when you loved me, this repayment is that today I and my companion come to eat!"

"I have forgotten the misfortune I suffered for you," Brigadier General Zhang replied, "If it were in my power, I would spend my fortune a second time for your glory."

Page 22

In a moment, Brigadier General Zhang thought that when he was rich, how he should have treated her if she had personally come to visit. Now, there was no valuable food in his house, and he was very anxious, but later he thought of a way to solve this difficulty.

Sure enough, the table was covered with a cloud-white tablecloth, a kind of timid memory; they had been glorious before, they all sat down and happily ate the roasted bird. After the meal, the woman thought it was time to announce the purpose of her visit.

"If you recall my previous coldness," she said, "undoubtedly, you will think I am so presumptuous to beg you. But if you know the power of a mother's love, I think you won't blame me either. My son saw your beloved falcon, which is your only bird, and he has become more haggard because he wants to get it. So I am here today to ask you to give that bird to my son as a gift, I am sure this can save my son."

Brigadier General Zhang began to cry sadly. Ping thought that this must be a sign that he was unwilling to give the bird. She was preparing to make further explanations, but Brigadier General Zhang said:

"Virtuous Madam, when I first decided to love you, fate was so cruel to me. But now that time has passed, you are condescending to come and see me. When I was rich, you never did this, perhaps never even thought of it, let alone ask me for a small gift. Fate is teasing me, so I don't have the power to grant your request. Now let me explain it to you simply.

"When you told me that you and your companion came to eat to honor me, I thought I should offer you every suitable food within my reach. Under this circumstance, I thought of this falcon, which you asked me for. It has a very noble physique, and is fat and docile, so I hid it this morning and roasted it as a delicacy for the banquet. Who knew that now you want this falcon to save your sick son, I have no ability to make you happy, sad me will never have a happy day."

Saying that, Brigadier General Zhang showed her the poor bird's feathers, beak, and claws. Ping blamed him for killing such a good falcon for a woman's lunch, and at the same time she praised his generosity in her heart.

The opportunity to get the falcon had been lost, and to restore her son's illness was even more disappointing, she said thank you and left Brigadier General Zhang. Her son stopped breathing soon after. She was heartbroken, she lived in an atmosphere of sorrow, until her brother hoped she would remarry to restore her spirits.

Ping didn't want to do this, but her brother persuaded her. Finally she said: "I am willing to remarry, but..." It seemed she recalled Brigadier General Zhang's generosity, "The person I am willing to marry is Brigadier General Zhang."

Her brother laughed and replied: "Why are you so stupid? Are you willing to marry a beggar?"

"Brother," she replied, "I would rather choose a man without money than a man with money."

Scientific Miscellany

The Mystery of the Electron 227

— Yang Bo

The atomic world, according to the discoveries of modern natural science, is considered a relatively old concept. Because the atom is considered the ultimate indivisible particle, and its decomposition and combination form all kinds of things, it can be said that all objects are atomic groups, and the entire world is just an atomic world. This is a hypothesis established by Democritus in ancient Greece, and it has been confirmed by modern natural science. However, the advancement of modern natural science has already led to the discovery of electrons by delving into the atom, knowing that the atom is not the ultimate indivisible particle. The atom itself is composed of even smaller electrons. This means that although the existence of atoms and the statement that all things are composed of them still hold, if we ask what the most basic particles that make up things are, the current answer can no longer be atoms, but should be electrons. The atomic worldview has changed to an electronic worldview, so people often call the current world the electric world. However, the so-called electric world, as understood by ordinary people, only means that current lighting, communication, talking, broadcasting, photography, driving, turning machines, etc., all use electricity, thus only understanding this term from the narrow perspective of applicability. In fact, this is not enough. The so-called electric world, if understood scientifically, is essentially a new philosophical worldview. Because flowing water, rocks, trees, animals, and even we humans ourselves, are just a mass of electricity, a group of electronic compounds! Of course, this is not to say that all things are just the accumulation of the quantity of electrons, in fact, the increase in quantity turns into various organic compounds, thus becoming various qualitatively different things, no longer simply the same nature as electrons. But the idea that all things are groups of electrons, that the world is an electronic world composed of electrons, is not shaken by this.

What is an electron? From a sensory point of view, it is a particle that cannot be touched or seen, because it is so small that it is inconceivable. A hydrogen bubble the size of the character '。' already contains hundreds of trillions of atoms, the smallness of atoms is amazing. But what about electrons? It is eighteen hundred times smaller than the smallest hydrogen atom, so it exceeds the range of what the body can feel even further than molecules and atoms. Although electrons are very small, their electric charge and mass have already been measured by the scientific community today in the United States. Milikan's measurement results show that the charge of an electron is: 4,774×10-10 electrostatic units, and its mass is: 9,0×10-28 grams, and its diameter is: 1,8×10-13 cm

The commonly referred to electron refers to the negative electron. In fact, electron simply refers to a particle with a certain unit of charge. Thus, electron includes both negative charge particles and positive charge particles, the former can be called a negative electron and the latter a positive electron. Electrons with the same properties are essentially no different. Ninety-two kinds of atoms are composed of these essentially undifferentiated electrons. Various atoms with different properties are simply the result of different numbers of electrons. For example, a hydrogen atom is composed of one positive electron as a core and one electron as a satellite, while a uranium atom is composed of two hundred and thirty positive electrons and one hundred and forty-six negative electrons forming the core, and ninety-two negative electrons as satellites, these are examples.

Regarding the nature of electrons, the current concept in the scientific community is still very chaotic. Most scientists say that an electron is only a group of electricity and has no real substance. Although they also admit that electrons have mass, they also say that this mass is not the so-called mass in the ordinary sense, that is, not the real and unchanging mass of matter. Therefore, Xiuneijie said in his "Outline of Atomic Structure": "What we usually call mass is the total amount of matter, without matter there is no mass, if there is mass there must be matter, and matter does not change due to position and speed, so mass has nothing to do with these. However, the conclusion of the essence of the electron is very different from this common sense, that is, the electron has mass but is not matter." However, strictly speaking, the current concept of the essence of electrons in the scientific community is incorrect. Mass without matter and electrons with only electricity but without a material basis cannot exist. Scraping away matter and only preserving electrical energy is a vitalist idealist point of view; admitting that electrons only have mass but no matter, then this mass becomes an empty conceptual entity, real matter becomes a simple concept in concept, which is also an idealist view of mass. This point of view shows the unscientific idealistic crisis of modern natural science in the epistemology of electrons.

The fundamental reason why modern natural scientists say that the mass of an electron is a non-material quantity is that the mass of an electron can change with its speed of motion. They always thought that the usual mass of matter does not change with changes in position, since the mass of electrons does not conform to this concept, it is considered
